title=".th">.th</a></li><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/.%E0%B9%84%E0%B8%97%E0%B8%A2" title=".&#3652;&#3607;&#3618;">.&#3652;&#3607;&#3618;</a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<table class="metadata mbox-small noprint selfref" role="presentation" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;width: 22em;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td class="mbox-image"><img alt="" data-file-height="50" data-file-width="200" decoding="async" height="10" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Thai_Alphabet_Sample.svg/40px-Thai_Alphabet_Sample.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Thai_Alphabet_Sample.svg/60px-Thai_Alphabet_Sample.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Thai_Alphabet_Sample.svg/80px-Thai_Alphabet_Sample.svg.png 2x" width="40"/></td>\n<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="vertical-align:middle; font-size:95%;">You may need <a href="/wiki/Help:Multilingual_support_(Indic)" title="Help:Multilingual support (Indic)">rendering support</a> to display the <a href="/wiki/Thai_language" title="Thai language">Thai text</a> in this article correctly.</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Thailand</b> (<a href="/wiki/Thai_language" title="Thai language">Thai</a>: <span lang="th">&#3611;&#3619;&#3632;&#3648;&#3607;&#3624;&#3652;&#3607;&#3618;</span>) (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'t\' in \'tie\'">t</span><span title="/a&#618;/: \'i\' in \'tide\'">a&#618;</span><span title="\'l\' in \'lie\'">l</span><span title="/&#230;/: \'a\' in \'bad\'">&#230;</span><span title="\'n\' in \'nigh\'">n</span><span title="\'d\' in \'dye\'">d</span></span>, <wbr/>-<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="\'l\' in \'lie\'">l</span><span title="/&#601;n/: \'on\' in \'button\'">&#601;n</span><span title="\'d\' in \'dye\'">d</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">TY</span>-land, -&#8288;l&#601;nd</i></a>), officially the <b>Kingdom of Thailand</b> and formerly known as <b>Siam</b> (<a href="/wiki/Thai_language" title="Thai language">Thai</a>: <span lang="th">&#3626;&#3618;&#3634;&#3617;</span>), is a country at the center of the <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asian</a> <a href="/wiki/Mainland_Southeast_Asia" title="Mainland Southeast Asia">Indochinese peninsula</a> composed of 76 <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Thailand" title="Provinces of Thailand">provinces</a>. At 513,120&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (198,120&#160;sq&#160;mi) and over 68 million people, Thailand is the world\'s <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area" title="List of countries and dependencies by area">50th largest country by total area</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population" title="List of countries and dependencies by population">21st-most-populous country</a>. The capital and largest city is <a href="/wiki/Bangkok" title="Bangkok">Bangkok</a>, a special administrative area. Thailand is bordered to the north by <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Laos" title="Laos">Laos</a>, to the east by Laos and <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodia</a>, to the south by the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Thailand" title="Gulf of Thailand">Gulf of Thailand</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, and to the west by the <a href="/wiki/Andaman_Sea" title="Andaman Sea">Andaman Sea</a> and the southern extremity of Myanmar. Its maritime boundaries include <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> in the Gulf of Thailand to the southeast, and <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> on the Andaman Sea to the southwest. Although nominally a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary democracy</a>, the most recent <a href="/wiki/2014_Thai_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="2014 Thai coup d\'&#233;tat">coup in 2014</a> established a <a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a> <a href="/wiki/Military_dictatorship" title="Military dictatorship">military dictatorship</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Tai_peoples" title="Tai peoples">Tai peoples</a> migrated from southwestern China to mainland <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> from the 11th century; the oldest known mention of their presence in the region by the <a href="/wiki/Exonym_and_endonym" title="Exonym and endonym">exonym</a> <i>Siamese</i> dates to the 12th century. Various <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indianised_kingdoms" title="Indianised kingdoms">Indianised kingdoms</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/Mon_kingdoms" title="Mon kingdoms">Mon</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Empire" title="Khmer Empire">Khmer Empire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Monarchies_of_Malaysia" title="Monarchies of Malaysia">Malay states</a> ruled the region, competing with Thai states such as <a href="/wiki/Ngoenyang" title="Ngoenyang">Ngoenyang</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sukhothai_Kingdom" title="Sukhothai Kingdom">Sukhothai Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lan_Na" title="Lan Na">Lan Na</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ayutthaya_Kingdom" title="Ayutthaya Kingdom">Ayutthaya Kingdom</a>, which rivaled each other. European contact began in 1511 with a Portuguese diplomatic mission to Ayutthaya, one of the great powers in the region. Ayutthaya reached its peak during cosmopolitan <a href="/wiki/Narai" title="Narai">Narai</a>\'s reign (1656&#8211;88), gradually declining thereafter until being ultimately destroyed in 1767 <a href="/wiki/Burmese%E2%80%93Siamese_War_(1765%E2%80%9367)" title="Burmese&#8211;Siamese War (1765&#8211;67)">in a war with Burma</a>. <a href="/wiki/Taksin" title="Taksin">Taksin</a> quickly reunified the fragmented territory and established the short-lived <a href="/wiki/Thonburi_Kingdom" title="Thonburi Kingdom">Thonburi Kingdom</a>. He was succeeded in 1782 by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddha_Yodfa_Chulaloke" title="Buddha Yodfa Chulaloke">Buddha Yodfa Chulaloke</a>, the first monarch of the <a href="/wiki/Chakri_dynasty" title="Chakri dynasty">Chakri dynasty</a> and founder of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rattanakosin_Kingdom" title="Rattanakosin Kingdom">Rattanakosin Kingdom</a>, which lasted into the early 20th century.\n</p><p>Through the 18th and 19th centuries, Siam faced pressure from France and the United Kingdom, including forced concessions of territory, but nevertheless it remained the only Southeast Asian country to avoid direct Western rule. Following a bloodless <a href="/wiki/Siamese_revolution_of_1932" title="Siamese revolution of 1932">revolution in 1932</a>, Siam became a constitutional monarchy and changed its official name to "Thailand". While it joined the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Allies_(World_War_I)" title="Allies (World War I)">Allies in World War I</a>, Thailand was an <a href="/wiki/Thailand_in_World_War_II" title="Thailand in World War II">Axis satellite</a> in <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. In the late 1950s, <a href="/wiki/Sarit_Thanarat" title="Sarit Thanarat">a military coup</a> revived the monarchy\'s historically influential role in politics. Thailand became a <a href="/wiki/Major_non-NATO_ally" title="Major non-NATO ally">major ally</a> of the United States and played a <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia_Treaty_Organization" title="Southeast Asia Treaty Organization">key anti-communist role in the region</a>. Apart from a <a href="/wiki/1973_Thai_popular_uprising" title="1973 Thai popular uprising">brief period of parliamentary democracy</a> in the mid-1970s, Thailand has periodically alternated between democracy and military rule. In the 21st century, Thailand endured a political crisis that culminated in two coups and the establishment of its <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Thailand#2017_Constitution" title="Constitution of Thailand">current and 20th constitution</a> by the military junta.\n</p><p>Thailand  is a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a> <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary</a> <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> under a <a href="/wiki/Military_dictatorship" title="Military dictatorship">military junta</a>. Thailand is a founding member of <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Southeast_Asian_Nations" title="Association of Southeast Asian Nations">Association of Southeast Asian Nations</a> and remains a major ally of the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Despite its comparatively sporadic changes in leadership, it is considered a <a href="/wiki/Regional_power" title="Regional power">regional power</a> in Southeast Asia and a <a href="/wiki/Middle_power" title="Middle power">middle power</a> in global affairs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> With a high level of <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">human development</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Thailand" title="Economy of Thailand">second largest economy</a> in Southeast Asia, and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP)">20th largest by PPP</a>, Thailand is classified as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newly_industrialized_economy" title="Newly industrialized economy">newly industrialized economy</a>; manufacturing, agriculture, and <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Thailand" title="Tourism in Thailand">tourism</a> are leading sectors of the economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-middleIncomeCountry_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-middleIncomeCountry-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GuardianThailandOverview_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-GuardianThailandOverview-18">[18]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2>\n<p>Thailand (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'t\' in \'nigh\'">n</span><span title="\'d\' in \'dye\'">d</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">TY</span>-land</i></a> or <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'t\' in \'tie\'">t</span><span title="/a&#618;/: \'i\' in \'tide\'">a&#618;</span><span title="\'l\' in \'lie\'">l</span><span title="/&#601;/: \'a\' in \'about\'">&#601;</span><span title="\'n\' in \'nigh\'">n</span><span title="\'d\' in \'dye\'">d</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">TY</span>-l&#601;nd</i></a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Thai_language" title="Thai language">Thai</a>: <span lang="th"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E0%B8%9B%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B0%E0%B9%80%E0%B8%97%E0%B8%A8%E0%B9%84%E0%B8%97%E0%B8%A2" title="wikt:&#3611;&#3619;&#3632;&#3648;&#3607;&#3624;&#3652;&#3607;&#3618;">&#3611;&#3619;&#3632;&#3648;&#3607;&#3624;&#3652;&#3607;&#3618;</a></span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Royal_Thai_General_System_of_Transcription" title="Royal Thai General System of Transcription">RTGS</a>:&#160;</small><span lang="th-Latn" style="font-style:inherit" title="Thai-language transliteration"><i>Prathet Thai</i></span>, <small>pronounced</small>&#160;<span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Thai_and_Lao" title="Help:IPA/Thai and Lao">[prat&#688;&#234;&#720;t t&#688;aj]</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Th-Thailand.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a></span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/06/Th-Thailand.ogg" title="Th-Thailand.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>), officially the Kingdom of Thailand (<a href="/wiki/Thai_language" title="Thai language">Thai</a>: <span lang="th"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B2%E0%B8%8A%E0%B8%AD%E0%B8%B2%E0%B8%93%E0%B8%B2%E0%B8%88%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%81%E0%B8%A3%E0%B9%84%E0%B8%97%E0%B8%A2" title="wikt:&#3619;&#3634;&#3594;&#3629;&#3634;&#3603;&#3634;&#3592;&#3633;&#3585;&#3619;&#3652;&#3607;&#3618;">&#3619;&#3634;&#3594;&#3629;&#3634;&#3603;&#3634;&#3592;&#3633;&#3585;&#3619;&#3652;&#3607;&#3618;</a></span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Royal_Thai_General_System_of_Transcription" title="Royal Thai General System of Transcription">RTGS</a>:&#160;</small><span lang="th-Latn" style="font-style:inherit" title="Thai-language transliteration"><i>Ratcha-anachak Thai</i></span> <small></small>&#160;<span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Thai_and_Lao" title="Help:IPA/Thai and Lao">[r&#226;&#720;tt&#865;&#597;&#688;a&#660;a&#720;na&#720;t&#865;&#597;&#224;k t&#688;aj]</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Th-pratheidthai_raachaanaajakthai.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="11" 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a></span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/77/Th-pratheidthai_raachaanaajakthai.ogg" title="Th-pratheidthai raachaanaajakthai.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh">&#27888;&#22269;</span>), formerly known as Siam (<a href="/wiki/Thai_language" title="Thai language">Thai</a>: <span lang="th"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%B2%E0%B8%A1" title="wikt:&#3626;&#3618;&#3634;&#3617;">&#3626;&#3618;&#3634;&#3617;</a></span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Royal_Thai_General_System_of_Transcription" title="Royal Thai General System of Transcription">RTGS</a>:&#160;</small><span lang="th-Latn" style="font-style:inherit" title="Thai-language transliteration"><i>Sayam</i></span> <small></small>&#160;<span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Thai_and_Lao" title="Help:IPA/Thai and Lao">[saj&#462;&#720;m]</a></span>), is a country at the centre of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indochinese_peninsula" title="Indochinese peninsula">Indochinese peninsula</a> in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Etymology_of_.22Siam.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id=\'Etymology_of_"Siam"\'>Etymology of "Siam"</span></h3>\n<p>The country has always been called <i><a href="/wiki/Mueang#Thailand" title="Mueang">Mueang Thai</a></i> by its citizens. By outsiders prior to 1949, it was usually known by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exonym" title="Exonym">exonym</a> <i>Siam</i> (<a href="/wiki/Thai_language" title="Thai language">Thai</a>: <span lang="th"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%B2%E0%B8%A1" title="wikt:&#3626;&#3618;&#3634;&#3617;">&#3626;&#3618;&#3634;&#3617;</a></span> <small><a href="/wiki/Royal_Thai_General_System_of_Transcription" title="Royal Thai General System of Transcription">RTGS</a>:&#160;</small><span lang="th-Latn" style="font-style:inherit" title="Thai-language transliteration">Sayam</span>, <small>pronounced</small>&#160;<span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Thai_and_Lao" title="Help:IPA/Thai and Lao">[saj&#462;&#720;m]</a></span>, also spelled <i>Siem</i>, <i>Sy&#226;m</i>, or <i>Sy&#226;ma</i>).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The word <i>Siam</i> may have originated from <a href="/wiki/Pali" title="Pali">Pali</a> (<i>suva&#7751;&#7751;abh&#363;mi</i>, &#8220;land of gold&#8221;) or <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> &#2358;&#2381;&#2351;&#2366;&#2350; (<i>&#347;y&#257;ma</i>, &#8220;dark&#8221;) or <a href="/wiki/Mon_language" title="Mon language">Mon</a> &#4123;&#4140;&#4121;&#4106;(<i>rhma&#241;&#241;a</i>, &#8220;stranger&#8221;). The names <i><a href="/wiki/Shan_people" title="Shan people">Shan</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Ahom_people" title="Ahom people">A-hom</a></i> seem to be variants of the same word. The word <i>&#346;y&#226;ma</i> is possibly not its origin, but a learned and artificial distortion.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (June 2015)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> Another theory is the name derives from Chinese: "Ayutthaya emerged as a dominant centre in the late fourteenth century. The Chinese called this region Xian, which the Portuguese converted into Siam." (Baker and Phongpaichit, A History of Thailand, 8)\nA further possibility is that <a href="/wiki/Mon_language" title="Mon language">Mon</a>-speaking peoples migrating south called themselves \'syem\' as do the autochthonous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mon-Khmer" title="Mon-Khmer">Mon-Khmer</a>-speaking inhabitants of the <a href="/wiki/Malay_Peninsula" title="Malay Peninsula">Malay Peninsula</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:King_Mongkut_(Rama_IV)_of_Siam_Signature_(English).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="148" data-file-width="612" decoding="async" height="53" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/King_Mongkut_%28Rama_IV%29_of_Siam_Signature_%28English%29.svg/220px-King_Mongkut_%28Rama_IV%29_of_Siam_Signature_%28English%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/King_Mongkut_%28Rama_IV%29_of_Siam_Signature_%28English%29.svg/330px-King_Mongkut_%28Rama_IV%29_of_Siam_Signature_%28English%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/King_Mongkut_%28Rama_IV%29_of_Siam_Signature_%28English%29.svg/440px-King_Mongkut_%28Rama_IV%29_of_Siam_Signature_%28English%29.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:King_Mongkut_(Rama_IV)_of_Siam_Signature_(English).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>SPPM Mongkut Rex Siamensium</i>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Mongkut" title="King Mongkut">King Mongkut</a>\'s signature</div></div></div>\n<p>The signature of King <a href="/wiki/Mongkut" title="Mongkut">Mongkut</a> (r. 1851&#8211;1868) reads <i>SPPM</i> (Somdet Phra Poramenthra Maha) <i>Mongkut King of the Siamese</i>, giving the name "Siam" official status until 24 June 1939 when it was changed to Thailand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ThaiCSM_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-ThaiCSM-21">[21]</a></sup> Thailand was renamed to Siam from 1946 to 1948, after which it again reverted to Thailand.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Etymology_of_.22Thailand.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id=\'Etymology_of_"Thailand"\'>Etymology of "Thailand"</span></h3>\n<p>According to <a href="/wiki/George_C%C5%93d%C3%A8s" title="George C&#339;d&#232;s">George C&#339;d&#232;s</a>, the word <i>Thai</i> (<a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E0%B9%84%E0%B8%97%E0%B8%A2" title="wikt:&#3652;&#3607;&#3618;">&#3652;&#3607;&#3618;</a>) means "free man" in the Thai language, "differentiating the Thai from the natives encompassed in Thai society as serfs".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEC&#339;d&#232;s1968197_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEC&#339;d&#232;s1968197-22">[22]</a></sup> A famous Thai scholar argued that Thai (<span lang="th" title="Thai language text">&#3652;&#3607;</span>) simply means "people" or "human being", since his investigation shows that in some rural areas the word "Thai" was used instead of the usual Thai word "khon" (<a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E0%B8%84%E0%B8%99" title="wikt:&#3588;&#3609;">&#3588;&#3609;</a>) for people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Michel_Ferlus" title="Michel Ferlus">Michel Ferlus</a>, the ethnonyms Thai/Tai (or Thay/Tay) would have evolved from the etymon <b>*k(&#601;)ri:</b> \'human being\' through the following chain: <b>*k&#601;ri:</b> &gt; <b>*k&#601;li:</b> &gt; <b>*k&#601;di:/*k&#601;daj</b> &gt; <b>*di:/*daj</b> &gt; <b>*daj<sup>A</sup></b> (Proto-Southwestern Tai) &gt; <b>t&#688;aj<sup>A2</sup></b> (in <a href="/wiki/Thai_language" title="Thai language">Siamese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lao_language" title="Lao language">Lao</a>) or &gt; <b>taj<sup>A2</sup></b> (in the other <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_Tai_languages" title="Southwestern Tai languages">Southwestern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_Tai_languages" title="Central Tai languages">Central Tai languages</a> classified by <a href="/wiki/Li_Fang-Kuei" title="Li Fang-Kuei">Li Fangkuei</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Michel_Furles_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Michel_Furles-24">[24]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Michel_Ferlus" title="Michel Ferlus">Michel Ferlus</a>\' work is based on some simple rules of phonetic change observable in the Sinosphere and studied for the most part by <a href="/wiki/William_H._Baxter" title="William H. Baxter">William H. Baxter</a> (1992).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fr&#233;d&#233;ric_Pain_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fr&#233;d&#233;ric_Pain-25">[25]</a></sup>\n</p><p>While Thai people will often refer to their country using the polite form <i>prathet Thai</i> (<a href="/wiki/Thai_language" title="Thai language">Thai</a>: <span lang="th">&#3611;&#3619;&#3632;&#3648;&#3607;&#3624;&#3652;&#3607;&#3618;</span>), they most commonly use the more colloquial term <i>mueang Thai</i> (<a href="/wiki/Thai_language" title="Thai language">Thai</a>: <span lang="th">&#3648;&#3617;&#3639;&#3629;&#3591;&#3652;&#3607;&#3618;</span>) or simply <i>Thai;</i> the word <i><a href="/wiki/Mueang" title="Mueang">mueang</a></i>, archaically referring to a city-state, is commonly used to refer to a city or town as the centre of a region. <i>Ratcha Anachak Thai</i> (<a href="/wiki/Thai_language" title="Thai language">Thai</a>: <span lang="th">&#3619;&#3634;&#3594;&#3629;&#3634;&#3603;&#3634;&#3592;&#3633;&#3585;&#3619;&#3652;&#3607;&#3618;</span>) means "kingdom of Thailand" or "kingdom of Thai". Etymologically, its components are: <i>ratcha</i> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sanskrit_language" title="Sanskrit language">Sanskrit</a>: <span lang="sa">&#2352;&#2366;&#2332;&#2344;&#2381;</span>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/R%C4%81jan" title="R&#257;jan">r&#257;jan</a></i>, "king, royal, realm"); <i>-ana-</i> (<a href="/wiki/Pali" title="Pali">Pali</a> <i>&#257;&#7751;&#257;</i> "authority, command, power", itself from the Sanskrit <span lang="sa" title="Sanskrit language text">&#2310;&#2332;&#2381;&#2334;&#2366;</span>, <i>&#257;j&#241;&#257;</i>, of the same meaning) <i>-chak</i> (from Sanskrit <span lang="sa" title="Sanskrit language text"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E0%A4%9A%E0%A4%95%E0%A5%8D%E0%A4%B0" title="wikt:&#2330;&#2325;&#2381;&#2352;">&#2330;&#2325;&#2381;&#2352;</a></span> <i>cakra-</i> "wheel", a symbol of power and rule). The <a href="/wiki/Thai_National_Anthem" title="Thai National Anthem">Thai National Anthem</a> (<a href="/wiki/Thai_language" title="Thai language">Thai</a>: <span lang="th">&#3648;&#3614;&#3621;&#3591;&#3594;&#3634;&#3605;&#3636;</span>), written by <a href="/wiki/Luang_Saranupraphan" title="Luang Saranupraphan">Luang Saranupraphan</a> during the extremely patriotic 1930s, refers to the Thai nation as <i>prathet Thai</i> (<a href="/wiki/Thai_language" title="Thai language">Thai</a>: <span lang="th">&#3611;&#3619;&#3632;&#3648;&#3607;&#3624;&#3652;&#3607;&#3618;</span>). The first line of the national anthem is: <i>prathet thai ruam lueat nuea chat chuea thai</i> (<a href="/wiki/Thai_language" title="Thai language">Thai</a>: <span lang="th">&#3611;&#3619;&#3632;&#3648;&#3607;&#3624;&#3652;&#3607;&#3618;&#3619;&#3623;&#3617;&#3648;&#3621;&#3639;&#3629;&#3604;&#3648;&#3609;&#3639;&#3657;&#3629;&#3594;&#3634;&#3605;&#3636;&#3648;&#3594;&#3639;&#3657;&#3629;&#3652;&#3607;&#3618;</span>), "Thailand is the unity of Thai flesh and blood."\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Thailand" title="History of Thailand">History of Thailand</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Prehistoric_Thailand" title="Prehistoric Thailand">Prehistoric Thailand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Early_history_of_Thailand" title="Early history of Thailand">Early history of Thailand</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tai_peoples" title="Tai peoples">Tai peoples</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TaiFamilyTree_Overlaid_On_Map.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2538" data-file-width="4004" decoding="async" height="190" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/TaiFamilyTree_Overlaid_On_Map.png/300px-TaiFamilyTree_Overlaid_On_Map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/TaiFamilyTree_Overlaid_On_Map.png/450px-TaiFamilyTree_Overlaid_On_Map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/TaiFamilyTree_Overlaid_On_Map.png/600px-TaiFamilyTree_Overlaid_On_Map.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TaiFamilyTree_Overlaid_On_Map.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map showing geographic distribution of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tai-Kadai_family" title="Tai-Kadai family">Tai-Kadai linguistic family</a>. Arrows represent general pattern of the migration of <a href="/wiki/Tai_peoples" title="Tai peoples">Tai-speaking tribes</a> along the rivers and over the lower passes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chris_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-chris-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>27</span></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>There is evidence of continued human habitation in present-day Thailand dated to 20,000 years before present.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-loc_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-loc-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>4</span></sup> Earliest evidence of rice growing was dated 2,000 BCE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chris_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-chris-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>4</span></sup> Bronze appeared during 1,250&#8211;1,000 BCE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chris_26-2"><a href="#cite_note-chris-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>4</span></sup> The site of <a href="/wiki/Ban_Chiang" title="Ban Chiang">Ban Chiang</a> in Northeast Thailand currently ranks as the earliest known center of copper and bronze production in Southeast Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Iron appeared around 500 BCE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chris_26-3"><a href="#cite_note-chris-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>5</span></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Funan" title="Kingdom of Funan">Kingdom of Funan</a> was the first and most powerful South East Asian kingdom at the time (2nd century BCE).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-loc_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-loc-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>5</span></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mon_people" title="Mon people">Mon people</a> established principalities of <a href="/wiki/Dvaravati" title="Dvaravati">Dvaravati</a> and kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Hariphunchai" title="Hariphunchai">Hariphunchai</a> in the 6th century. <a href="/wiki/Khmer_people" title="Khmer people">Khmer people</a> established <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khmer_empire" title="Khmer empire">Khmer empire</a> centered in <a href="/wiki/Angkor" title="Angkor">Angkor</a> in the 9th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-loc_27-2"><a href="#cite_note-loc-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>7</span></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tambralinga" title="Tambralinga">Tambralinga</a>, a Malay state controlling trade through Malacca Strait, rose in the 10th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-loc_27-3"><a href="#cite_note-loc-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>5</span></sup> Indochina peninsula was heavily influenced by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indianized_kingdom" title="Indianized kingdom">culture and religions of India</a>, starting with the Kingdom of Funan to the Khmer Empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Thai_people" title="Thai people">Thai people</a> are in <a href="/wiki/Tai_peoples" title="Tai peoples">Tai ethnic group</a>, which were characterized by common linguistic roots.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wyatt_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-wyatt-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>2</span></sup> Chinese chronicles first mentioned Tai peoples in 6th century BC. While there are many assumptions regarding the origin of Tai peoples, <a href="/wiki/David_K._Wyatt" title="David K. Wyatt">David K. Wyatt</a>, a prominent historian on Thailand, argued that their ancestors which at the present inhabit Laos, Thailand, Myanmar, India and China came from <a href="/wiki/%C4%90i%E1%BB%87n_Bi%C3%AAn_Ph%E1%BB%A7" title="&#272;i&#7879;n Bi&#234;n Ph&#7911;">&#272;i&#7879;n Bi&#234;n Ph&#7911;</a> area around 5th and 8th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wyatt_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-wyatt-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>6</span></sup> Thai people began migrating into present-day Thailand around 11th century, which Mon and Khmer people occupied at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brihis_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-brihis-31">[31]</a></sup> Thus Thai culture was influenced by Indian, Mon and Khmer cultures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to French historian <a href="/wiki/George_C%C5%93d%C3%A8s" title="George C&#339;d&#232;s">George C&#339;d&#232;s</a>, "The Thai first enter history of <a href="/wiki/Farther_India" title="Farther India">Farther India</a> in the eleventh century with the mention of <i>Syam</i> slaves or prisoners of war in" <a href="/wiki/Champa" title="Champa">Champa</a> epigraphy, and "in the twelfth century, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bas-relief" title="Bas-relief">bas-reliefs</a> of <a href="/wiki/Angkor_Wat" title="Angkor Wat">Angkor Wat</a>" where "a group of warriors" are described as <i>Syam</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEC&#339;d&#232;s1968190&#8211;191,194&#8211;195_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEC&#339;d&#232;s1968190&#8211;191,194&#8211;195-33">[33]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_states">Early states</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Initial_states_of_Thailand" title="Initial states of Thailand">Initial states of Thailand</a></div>\n<p>After the decline of the Khmer Empire and <a href="/wiki/Pagan_Kingdom" title="Pagan Kingdom">Kingdom of Pagan</a> in the early 13th century, various states thrived in their place. The domains of Tai people existed from the northeast of present-day India to the north of present-day Laos and to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Malay_peninsula" title="Malay peninsula">Malay peninsula</a>. During the 13th century, Tai people have already settled in the core land of <a href="/wiki/Dvaravati" title="Dvaravati">Dvaravati</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lavo_Kingdom" title="Lavo Kingdom">Lavo Kingdom</a> to <a href="/wiki/Nakhon_Si_Thammarat_Kingdom" title="Nakhon Si Thammarat Kingdom">Nakhon Si Thammarat</a> in the south. There are, however, no records detailing the arrival of the Tais. Around 1240s, <a href="/wiki/Si_Inthrathit" title="Si Inthrathit">Pho Khun Bang Klang Hao</a>, a local Tai ruler, rallied the people to rebel against the Khmer. He later crowned himself the first king of <a href="/wiki/Sukhothai_Kingdom" title="Sukhothai Kingdom">Sukhothai Kingdom</a> in 1238. Mainstream Thai historians count Sukhothai as the first kingdom of Thai people. Sukhothai expanded furthest during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Ram_Khamhaeng" title="Ram Khamhaeng">Ram Khamhaeng</a> (1279&#8211;98). However, it was mostly a network of local lords who swore fealty to Sukhothai, not directly controlled by it. He is believed to invent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thai_script" title="Thai script">Thai script</a> and Thai ceramics was an important export goods in his era. Sukhothai embraced <a href="/wiki/Theravada" title="Theravada">Theravada</a> <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> in the reign of <a href="/wiki/Maha_Thammaracha_I" title="Maha Thammaracha I">Maha Thammaracha I</a> (1347&#8211;68).\n</p><p>To the north, <a href="/wiki/Mangrai" title="Mangrai">Mangrai</a> who descended from a local ruler linage of <a href="/wiki/Ngoenyang" title="Ngoenyang">Ngoenyang</a>, founded the kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Lan_Na" title="Lan Na">Lan Na</a> in 1292, centered in <a href="/wiki/Chiang_Mai" title="Chiang Mai">Chiang Mai</a>. He unified the surrounding area and his dynasty would rule the kingdom continuously for the next two centuries. He also created a network of state through political alliance to the east and north of <a href="/wiki/Mekong" title="Mekong">Mekong</a>. While in the port in Lower Chao Phraya Basin, a federation around <a href="/wiki/Phetchaburi" title="Phetchaburi">Phetchaburi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suphan_Buri" title="Suphan Buri">Suphan Buri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lopburi" title="Lopburi">Lopburi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ayutthaya_Kingdom" title="Ayutthaya Kingdom">Ayutthaya</a> area was created in the 11th century.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ayutthaya_Kingdom">Ayutthaya Kingdom</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Ayutthaya_Kingdom" title="Ayutthaya Kingdom">Ayutthaya Kingdom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thonburi_Kingdom" title="Thonburi Kingdom">Thonburi Kingdom</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Southeast_Asian_history_-_Around_1540.png"><img alt="Southeast Asia around 1540" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1189" data-file-width="755" decoding="async" height="346" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Southeast_Asian_history_-_Around_1540.png/220px-Southeast_Asian_history_-_Around_1540.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Southeast_Asian_history_-_Around_1540.png/330px-Southeast_Asian_history_-_Around_1540.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Southeast_Asian_history_-_Around_1540.png/440px-Southeast_Asian_history_-_Around_1540.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Southeast_Asian_history_-_Around_1540.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ayutthaya\'s zone of influence and neighbours, c. 1540</div></div></div>\n<p>According to the most widely accepted version of its origin, Ayutthaya Kingdom rose from the earlier, nearby <a href="/wiki/Lavo_Kingdom" title="Lavo Kingdom">Lavo Kingdom</a> and Suvarnabhumi with <a href="/wiki/Uthong" title="Uthong">Uthong</a> as its first king. Ayutthaya was a patchwork of self-governing principalities and tributary provinces owing allegiance to the king of Ayutthaya under <a href="/wiki/Mandala_(political_model)" title="Mandala (political model)">mandala system</a>. Its initial expansion is through conquest and political marriage. Before the end of the 15th century, Ayutthaya invaded Khmer Empire twice and sacked its capital <a href="/wiki/Angkor" title="Angkor">Angkor</a>. Ayutthaya then became a regional great power in place of Khmer Empire. Constant interference of Sukhothai effectively made it a vassal state of Ayutthaya and was finally incorporated in to the kingdom. <a href="/wiki/Borommatrailokkanat" title="Borommatrailokkanat">Borommatrailokkanat</a> brought about bureaucratic reforms which lasted into the 20th century and created a system of social hierarchy called <i><a href="/wiki/Sakdina" title="Sakdina">Sakdina</a></i>, where common male was conscripted into <a href="/wiki/Corv%C3%A9e" title="Corv&#233;e">corv&#233;e</a> for six months a year. Ayutthaya was interested in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Malay_peninsula" title="Malay peninsula">Malay peninsula</a> but failed to conquer <a href="/wiki/Malacca_Sultanate" title="Malacca Sultanate">Malacca Sultanate</a> which was supported by Chinese <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ming_Dynasty" title="Ming Dynasty">Ming Dynasty</a>.\n</p><p>European contact and trade started in the early 16th century, with the <a href="/wiki/Duarte_Fernandes" title="Duarte Fernandes">envoy</a> of <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a> duke <a href="/wiki/Afonso_de_Albuquerque" title="Afonso de Albuquerque">Afonso de Albuquerque</a> in 1511, followed by the French, Dutch, and English. Rivalry for supremacy over Chiang Mai and Mon people pitted Ayutthaya against Burmese Kingdom. Multiple war with its ruling dynasty <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taungoo_Dynasty" title="Taungoo Dynasty">Taungoo Dynasty</a> starting in the 1540s in the reign of <a href="/wiki/Tabinshwehti" title="Tabinshwehti">Tabinshwehti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bayinnaung" title="Bayinnaung">Bayinnaung</a> were ultimately ended with <a href="/wiki/Burmese%E2%80%93Siamese_War_(1568%E2%80%9370)" title="Burmese&#8211;Siamese War (1568&#8211;70)">capture of the capital in 1570</a>. Then was a period of brief vassalage to Burma until <a href="/wiki/Naresuan" title="Naresuan">Naresuan</a> proclaimed independence in 1584.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AMH-5626-NA_Bird%27s_eye_view_of_the_city_of_Judja.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1591" data-file-width="2400" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/AMH-5626-NA_Bird%27s_eye_view_of_the_city_of_Judja.jpg/220px-AMH-5626-NA_Bird%27s_eye_view_of_the_city_of_Judja.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/AMH-5626-NA_Bird%27s_eye_view_of_the_city_of_Judja.jpg/330px-AMH-5626-NA_Bird%27s_eye_view_of_the_city_of_Judja.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/AMH-5626-NA_Bird%27s_eye_view_of_the_city_of_Judja.jpg/440px-AMH-5626-NA_Bird%27s_eye_view_of_the_city_of_Judja.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AMH-5626-NA_Bird%27s_eye_view_of_the_city_of_Judja.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Painting by <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Vingboons" title="Johannes Vingboons">Johannes Vingboons</a> of Ayutthaya, c. 1665</div></div></div>\n<p>Ayutthaya then seek to improve relations with European powers for many successive reigns. The kingdom especially prospered during cosmopolitan <a href="/wiki/Narai" title="Narai">Narai</a>\'s reign (1656&#8211;88) where some European travelers regarded Ayutthaya as Asian great powers alongside China and India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chris_26-4"><a href="#cite_note-chris-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>ix</span></sup> However, growing French influence later in his reign was met with nationalist sentiment and led eventually to the <a href="/wiki/Siamese_revolution_of_1688" title="Siamese revolution of 1688">revolution of 1688</a>. However, overall relations remain stable with French missionaries still active in preaching Christianity.\n</p><p>After that, there was a period of relative peace but the kingdom\'s influence gradually waned, partly because of bloody struggles over each succession, until the capital Ayutthaya was <a href="/wiki/Burmese%E2%80%93Siamese_War_(1765%E2%80%9367)" title="Burmese&#8211;Siamese War (1765&#8211;67)">utterly destroyed in 1767</a> by Burma\'s new <a href="/wiki/Alaungpaya" title="Alaungpaya">Alaungpaya</a> dynasty. Anarchy followed destruction of the former capital, with its territories split into five different factions, each controlled by a warlord. <a href="/wiki/Taksin" title="Taksin">Taksin</a> rose to power and proclaimed <a href="/wiki/Thonburi" title="Thonburi">Thonburi</a> as temporary capital in the same year. He also quickly subdued the other warlords. His forces engaged in wars with Burma, Laos, and Cambodia, which successfully drove the Burmese out of Lan Na in 1775, captured <a href="/wiki/Vientiane" title="Vientiane">Vientiane</a> in 1778 and tried to install a pro-Thai king in Cambodia in the 1770s. In his final years there was a coup which was caused by his supposedly "insanity," and eventually Taksin and his sons were executed by longtime companion General <a href="/wiki/Rama_I" title="Rama I">Chao Phraya Chakri</a> (future Rama I). He was the first king of the ruling <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chakri_Dynasty" title="Chakri Dynasty">Chakri Dynasty</a> and founder of <a href="/wiki/Bangkok" title="Bangkok">Bangkok</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rattanakosin_Kingdom" title="Rattanakosin Kingdom">Rattanakosin Kingdom</a>) on April 6, 1782.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modernization_and_centralization">Modernization and centralization</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rattanakosin_Kingdom" title="Rattanakosin Kingdom">Rattanakosin Kingdom</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Siamese_territorial_concessions_(1867-1909)_with_flags.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="514" data-file-width="301" decoding="async" height="376" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Siamese_territorial_concessions_%281867-1909%29_with_flags.gif/220px-Siamese_territorial_concessions_%281867-1909%29_with_flags.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/91/Siamese_territorial_concessions_%281867-1909%29_with_flags.gif 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Siamese_territorial_concessions_(1867-1909)_with_flags.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Siamese territorial concessions to Britain and France by year</div></div></div>\n<p>Under <a href="/wiki/Rama_I" title="Rama I">Rama I</a> (1782&#8211;1809), Rattanakosin successfully defended against Burmese attacks and put an end to Burmese invasion. He also created overlordship over large portions of Laos and Cambodia. In 1821, <a href="/wiki/John_Crawfurd" title="John Crawfurd">John Crawfurd</a> was sent on a mission to negotiate a new trade agreement with Siam &#8212; the first sign of an issue which was to dominate 19th-century Siamese politics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Bangkok signed <a href="/wiki/Burney_Treaty" title="Burney Treaty">Burney Treaty</a> in 1826, after the British victory in <a href="/wiki/First_Anglo-Burmese_War" title="First Anglo-Burmese War">First Anglo-Burmese War</a>. <a href="/wiki/Anouvong" title="Anouvong">Anouvong</a> of Vientiane, who misunderstood that Britain was about to attack Bangkok, started the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lao_rebellion_(1826%E2%80%9328)" title="Lao rebellion (1826&#8211;28)">Lao rebellion</a> in 1826 and was defeated. Vientiane was destroyed and a large number of Lao people was relocated to <a href="/wiki/Khorat_Plateau" title="Khorat Plateau">Khorat Plateau</a> as the result. Bangkok also waged <a href="/wiki/Siamese%E2%80%93Vietnamese_wars" title="Siamese&#8211;Vietnamese wars">multiple wars with Vietnam</a>, where Bangkok successfully regained influence over Cambodia.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:King_and_Tsar.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="592" decoding="async" height="284" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/King_and_Tsar.jpg/210px-King_and_Tsar.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/King_and_Tsar.jpg/315px-King_and_Tsar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/King_and_Tsar.jpg/420px-King_and_Tsar.jpg 2x" width="210"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:King_and_Tsar.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>King <a href="/wiki/Chulalongkorn" title="Chulalongkorn">Chulalongkorn</a> with Tsar <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nicholas_II" title="Nicholas II">Nicholas II</a> in Saint Petersburg, during his first Grand Tour in 1897</div></div></div>\n<p>Since the late 19th century, Siam tried to subdue the ethnic groups in the realm as colony. In the reign of <a href="/wiki/Mongkut" title="Mongkut">Mongkut</a> (1851&#8211;68), who recognized the threat of Western powers, the court contacted the British government directly to defuse the tension. A British mission led by Sir <a href="/wiki/John_Bowring" title="John Bowring">John Bowring</a>, Governor of Hong Kong, led to the conclusion of <a href="/wiki/Bowring_Treaty" title="Bowring Treaty">Bowring Treaty</a>, first of many <a href="/wiki/Unequal_treaty" title="Unequal treaty">unequal treaties</a> with Western countries. It, however, brought economic development in Bangkok and international trade. The unexpected death of Mongkut by <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a> led to succession by young <a href="/wiki/Chulalongkorn" title="Chulalongkorn">Prince Chulalongkorn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Somdet_Chaophraya_Sri_Suriwongse" title="Somdet Chaophraya Sri Suriwongse">Somdet Chaophraya Sri Suriwongse</a> (Chuang Bunnag) acted as a regent.\n</p><p>Chulalongkorn (r. 1868&#8211;1910) initiated centralization, set up a privy council, and abolished slavery and <a href="/wiki/Corv%C3%A9e" title="Corv&#233;e">corv&#233;e</a> system. <a href="/wiki/Front_Palace_crisis" title="Front Palace crisis">Front Palace crisis</a> of 1874 stalled reformation attempt. In the 1870s and 1880s, he incorporated the protectorate up north into the kingdom proper, which later expanded to the protectorate in the northeast and the south. He established twelve <i>krom</i> in 1888, which was equivalent to present-day ministries. <a href="/wiki/Franco-Siamese_War" title="Franco-Siamese War">Crisis of 1893</a> which was caused by French demands of Laotian territory east of Mekong. France and Britain agreed between themselves to make Siam <a href="/wiki/Buffer_state" title="Buffer state">buffer state</a>. It was not until the 20th century can Siam renegotiate every unequal treaty since Bowring treaty, including <a href="/wiki/Extraterritoriality" title="Extraterritoriality">extraterritoriality</a>, but had to pay with many territorial exchanges. The advent of monthon system marked the creation of modern nation-state. In 1905, there was rebellions in ancient Pattani area, Ubon Ratchathani and Phrae to oppose an attempt to subdue the power of local ruling lords.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Palace_Revolt_of_1912" title="Palace Revolt of 1912">Palace Revolt of 1912</a> was a failed attempt by Western-educated military officers who aimed to overthrow absolute monarchy. <a href="/wiki/Vajiravudh" title="Vajiravudh">Vajiravudh</a> (r. 1910&#8211;25) responded by propaganda for the entirety of his reign. He promoted the <a href="/wiki/Thaification" title="Thaification">idea of Thai nation</a>. In 1917, Siam joined <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> on the side of <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">the Allies</a> because there were concerns that the Allies may react to neutral countries and desire to amend past unequal treaties. In the aftermath Siam joined <a href="/wiki/Paris_Peace_Conference,_1919" title="Paris Peace Conference, 1919">Paris Peace Conference</a>, gained freedom of taxation and cancellation of extraterritoriality.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Constitutional_monarchy.2C_World_War_II.2C_and_Cold_War"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Constitutional_monarchy,_World_War_II,_and_Cold_War">Constitutional monarchy, World War II, and Cold War</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Thailand_in_World_War_II" title="Thailand in World War II">Thailand in World War II</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_Thailand_(1932%E2%80%9373)" title="History of Thailand (1932&#8211;73)">History of Thailand (1932&#8211;73)</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Siamese_revolution_of_1932" title="Siamese revolution of 1932">bloodless revolution</a> took place in 1932, carried out by the <a href="/wiki/Khana_Ratsadon" title="Khana Ratsadon">Khana Ratsadon</a> group of military and civilian officials resulted in a transition of power, when <a href="/wiki/Prajadhipok" title="Prajadhipok">Prajadhipok</a> was forced to grant the people of Siam their first constitution, thereby ending centuries of <a href="/wiki/Absolute_monarchy" title="Absolute monarchy">absolute monarchy</a>. It was the combined results of economic hardship felt by the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>, sharply fell rice price and significantly reduction in public spending causing discontent among aristocrats. In 1933, <a href="/wiki/Boworadet_rebellion" title="Boworadet rebellion">A counter-revolutionary rebellion</a> occurred which aimed to reinstate absolute monarchy but failed. Prajadhipok\'s conflict with the government eventually led to abdication. The government selected <a href="/wiki/Ananda_Mahidol" title="Ananda Mahidol">Ananda Mahidol</a>, who was studying in Switzerland, to be the new king.\n</p><p>Later that decade, the military wing of Khana Ratsadon came to dominate Siamese politics. <a href="/wiki/Plaek_Phibunsongkhram" title="Plaek Phibunsongkhram">Plaek Phibunsongkhram</a> who became premier in 1938, started political oppression and took openly anti-royalist stance. His government adopted nationalism and Westernization, anti-Chinese and anti-French policies. In 1940, there was a decree changing the name of the country from "Siam" to "Thailand." In 1941, Thailand was in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French%E2%80%93Thai_War" title="French&#8211;Thai War">a brief conflict</a> with <a href="/wiki/Vichy_France" title="Vichy France">Vichy France</a> resulting in Thailand gained Laotian and Cambodian territories until the war ends. On December 8, 1941 Japan invaded Thailand and the government quickly agreed to join military alliance with Japan. The government also declare war on the United States and the United Kingdom. <a href="/wiki/Free_Thai_Movement" title="Free Thai Movement">Free Thai Movement</a> was launched both in Thailand and abroad to oppose the government and Japanese occupation. After the war ends in 1945 Thailand signed formal agreement to end the state of war with <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">the Allies</a>. Most Allied powers did not recognize Thailand\'s declaration of war.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:King_Rama_IX_being_presented_with_regalia_at_coronation.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="2250" decoding="async" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/King_Rama_IX_being_presented_with_regalia_at_coronation.jpg/150px-King_Rama_IX_being_presented_with_regalia_at_coronation.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/King_Rama_IX_being_presented_with_regalia_at_coronation.jpg/225px-King_Rama_IX_being_presented_with_regalia_at_coronation.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/King_Rama_IX_being_presented_with_regalia_at_coronation.jpg/300px-King_Rama_IX_being_presented_with_regalia_at_coronation.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:King_Rama_IX_being_presented_with_regalia_at_coronation.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Coronation of King <a href="/wiki/Bhumibol_Adulyadej" title="Bhumibol Adulyadej">Bhumibol Adulyadej</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>In June 1946, young King Ananda was found dead under mysterious circumstances. His younger brother <a href="/wiki/Bhumibol_Adulyadej" title="Bhumibol Adulyadej">Bhumibol Adulyadej</a> succeeded the throne. Thailand signed <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia_Treaty_Organization" title="Southeast Asia Treaty Organization">Southeast Asia Treaty Organization</a> (SEATO) to became an active ally of the United States since 1954. Field Marshal <a href="/wiki/Sarit_Thanarat" title="Sarit Thanarat">Sarit Thanarat</a> launched a coup in 1957, which removed Khana Ratsadon from politics. His rule was autocratic; he built his legitimacy around the god-like status of the monarch and by channeling the government\'s loyalty to the king. His government improved the country\'s infrastructure and education. After the US joined <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a> in 1961, there was a secret agreement where the US promised to protect Thailand.\n</p><p>The period brought about increasing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Modernisation" title="Modernisation">modernisation</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Westernisation" title="Westernisation">Westernisation</a>. Internal conflict regarding economic difficulties which began in 1968 led to <a href="/wiki/1973_Thai_popular_uprising" title="1973 Thai popular uprising">1973 Thai popular uprising</a>, an important event in Thai modern history.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary_history">Contemporary history</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Thailand_(1973%E2%80%932001)" title="History of Thailand (1973&#8211;2001)">History of Thailand (1973&#8211;2001)</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Thailand_since_2001" title="History of Thailand since 2001">History of Thailand since 2001</a></div>\n<p>Constant unrest and instability, as well as fear of communist takeover after <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Saigon" title="Fall of Saigon">Fall of Saigon</a>, made some ultra-right groups brand increasingly leftist students as communists. This culminated in <a href="/wiki/Thammasat_University_massacre" title="Thammasat University massacre">Thammasat University massacre</a> in October 1976. A coup d\'&#233;tat on that very day brought Thailand a new ultra-right government, which oppressed many media outlets, officials, and intellectuals, and fueled the <a href="/wiki/Communist_insurgency_in_Thailand" title="Communist insurgency in Thailand">Communist insurgency</a> further. Another coup in the following year installed a more moderate government, which offered amnesty to communist fighters in 1978. The Party abandoned the insurgency by 1983. Thailand had its first elected Prime Minister in 1988.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bri31_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-bri31-35">[35]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Suchinda_Kraprayoon" title="Suchinda Kraprayoon">Suchinda Kraprayoon</a>, who was <a href="/wiki/National_Peace_Keeping_Council" title="National Peace Keeping Council">the coup leader in 1991</a> and said he would not seek to become Prime Minister, was nominated as one by majority coalition government after the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thai_general_election,_March_1992" title="Thai general election, March 1992">1992 general election</a>. This caused a popular demonstration in Bangkok, which ended with <a href="/wiki/Black_May_(1992)" title="Black May (1992)">a military crackdown</a>. Bhumibol intervened in the event and Suchinda then resigned.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2010_09_19_red_shirt_protest_bkk_09.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1050" data-file-width="1920" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/2010_09_19_red_shirt_protest_bkk_09.JPG/220px-2010_09_19_red_shirt_protest_bkk_09.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/2010_09_19_red_shirt_protest_bkk_09.JPG/330px-2010_09_19_red_shirt_protest_bkk_09.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/2010_09_19_red_shirt_protest_bkk_09.JPG/440px-2010_09_19_red_shirt_protest_bkk_09.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2010_09_19_red_shirt_protest_bkk_09.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/United_Front_for_Democracy_Against_Dictatorship" title="United Front for Democracy Against Dictatorship">United Front for Democracy Against Dictatorship</a>, Red Shirts, <a href="/wiki/2010_Thai_political_protests" title="2010 Thai political protests">protest</a> in 2010</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/1997_Asian_financial_crisis" title="1997 Asian financial crisis">1997 Asian financial crisis</a> originated in Thailand and forced the country to take an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IMF" title="IMF">IMF</a> loan with unpopular provisions. The populist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thai_Rak_Thai" title="Thai Rak Thai">Thai Rak Thai</a> party, led by prime minister <a href="/wiki/Thaksin_Shinawatra" title="Thaksin Shinawatra">Thaksin Shinawatra</a>, governed from 2001 until 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/South_Thailand_insurgency" title="South Thailand insurgency">South Thailand insurgency</a> escalated starting from 2004. The <a href="/wiki/2004_Indian_Ocean_earthquake_and_tsunami" title="2004 Indian Ocean earthquake and tsunami">2004 Indian Ocean earthquake and tsunami</a> hit the country, mostly in the south. Massive protests against Thaksin, led by the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Alliance_for_Democracy" title="People\'s Alliance for Democracy">People\'s Alliance for Democracy</a> (PAD), ended with <a href="/wiki/2006_Thai_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="2006 Thai coup d\'&#233;tat">a coup d\'&#233;tat in 2006</a>.\n</p><p>In 2007, a civilian government led by the Thaksin-allied <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Power_Party_(Thailand)" title="People\'s Power Party (Thailand)">People\'s Power Party</a> (PPP) was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thai_general_election,_2007" title="Thai general election, 2007">elected</a>. <a href="/wiki/2008_Thai_political_crisis" title="2008 Thai political crisis">Another protest led by PAD</a> ended with the dissolution of PPP, and the <a href="/wiki/Democrat_Party_(Thailand)" title="Democrat Party (Thailand)">Democrat Party</a> led a coalition government in its place. The pro-Thaksin <a href="/wiki/United_Front_for_Democracy_Against_Dictatorship" title="United Front for Democracy Against Dictatorship">United Front for Democracy Against Dictatorship</a> (UDD) protested both <a href="/wiki/2009_Thai_political_unrest" title="2009 Thai political unrest">in 2009</a> and <a href="/wiki/2010_Thai_political_protests" title="2010 Thai political protests">in 2010</a>.\n</p><p>After <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thai_general_election,_2011" title="Thai general election, 2011">the general election of 2011</a>, the populist <a href="/wiki/Pheu_Thai_Party" title="Pheu Thai Party">Pheu Thai Party</a> won a majority and <a href="/wiki/Yingluck_Shinawatra" title="Yingluck Shinawatra">Yingluck Shinawatra</a>, Thaksin\'s younger sister, became Prime Minister. The <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Democratic_Reform_Committee" title="People\'s Democratic Reform Committee">People\'s Democratic Reform Committee</a> organized <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%932014_Thai_political_crisis" title="2013&#8211;2014 Thai political crisis">another anti-Shinawatra protest</a>, which ended with <a href="/wiki/2014_Thai_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="2014 Thai coup d\'&#233;tat">another coup d\'&#233;tat in 2014</a>, and democracy was replaced with what the rulers called "National Harmony."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup>  The <a href="/wiki/National_Council_for_Peace_and_Order" title="National Council for Peace and Order">National Council for Peace and Order</a>, a military junta led by General <a href="/wiki/Prayut_Chan-o-cha" title="Prayut Chan-o-cha">Prayut Chan-o-cha</a>, has led the country since. The referendum and adoption of Thailand\'s current constitution happened under the junta\'s rule. In 2016 Bhumibol, the longest reigning Thai king, died, and his son <a href="/wiki/Vajiralongkorn" title="Vajiralongkorn">Vajiralongkorn</a> ascended the throne. In 2019 the king\'s sister, <a href="/wiki/Ubol_Ratana" title="Ubol Ratana">Ubolratana Rajakanya Sirivadhana Varnavadi</a>, was nominated to be a candidate for prime minister by a political party associated with the Shinawatra political family. The king however dismissed the nomination as "inappropriate" behaviour that went against the nation\'s constitutional monarchy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-38">[38]</a></sup> Also declaring his candidacy was ruling Prime Minister Prayuth Chan-ocha, a defender of the Thai monarchy. He was backed by the military led <a href="/wiki/Phalang_Pracharat_Party" title="Phalang Pracharat Party">Palang Pracharat Party</a>. The ruling junta restricts freedom of speech and assembly. Those who violate, or who are seen to be political opponents to the ruling party members, are sent to "attitude adjustment " camps. In addition, citizens who insult the monarchy are subject to strict  <a href="/wiki/L%C3%A8se-majest%C3%A9" title="L&#232;se-majest&#233;">l&#232;se-majest&#233;</a> laws. Prosecution under these laws that make it a crime to criticize or insult the king have increased significantly in recent years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-38">[38]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_and_government">Politics and government</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Thailand" title="Politics of Thailand">Politics of Thailand</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constitutions_of_Thailand" title="Constitutions of Thailand">Constitutions of Thailand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Thailand" title="Law of Thailand">Law of Thailand</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Thailand" title="Government of Thailand">Government of Thailand</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Meeting_with_Prime_Minister_of_Thailand_Yingluck_Shinawatra_and_Vladimir_Putin_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="678" data-file-width="1100" decoding="async" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Meeting_with_Prime_Minister_of_Thailand_Yingluck_Shinawatra_and_Vladimir_Putin_01.jpg/220px-Meeting_with_Prime_Minister_of_Thailand_Yingluck_Shinawatra_and_Vladimir_Putin_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Meeting_with_Prime_Minister_of_Thailand_Yingluck_Shinawatra_and_Vladimir_Putin_01.jpg/330px-Meeting_with_Prime_Minister_of_Thailand_Yingluck_Shinawatra_and_Vladimir_Putin_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Meeting_with_Prime_Minister_of_Thailand_Yingluck_Shinawatra_and_Vladimir_Putin_01.jpg/440px-Meeting_with_Prime_Minister_of_Thailand_Yingluck_Shinawatra_and_Vladimir_Putin_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Meeting_with_Prime_Minister_of_Thailand_Yingluck_Shinawatra_and_Vladimir_Putin_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Thailand\'s Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Yingluck_Shinawatra" title="Yingluck Shinawatra">Yingluck Shinawatra</a> was removed from office on 7 May 2014 by a controversial Constitutional Court decision.</div></div></div>\n<p>Prior to 1932, all legislative powers were vested in the monarch. This had been the case since the foundation of the <a href="/wiki/Sukhothai_Kingdom" title="Sukhothai Kingdom">Sukhothai Kingdom</a> in the 12th century as the king was seen as a "Dharmaraja" or "king who rules in accordance with <a href="/wiki/Dharma" title="Dharma">Dharma</a>", (the Buddhist law of righteousness). Modern <a href="/wiki/Absolute_monarchy" title="Absolute monarchy">absolute monarchy</a> was established by Chulalongkorn when he transformed the decentralized protectorate system into a unitary state. On 24 June 1932, <a href="/wiki/Khana_Ratsadon" title="Khana Ratsadon">Khana Ratsadon</a> (People\'s Party) carried out a bloodless revolution which ended the absolute rule.\n</p><p>The politics of Thailand is conducted within the framework of a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a>, whereby the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Thailand" title="Prime Minister of Thailand">Prime Minister</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Hereditary_monarchy" title="Hereditary monarchy">hereditary monarch</a> is <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judiciary</a> is supposed to be independent of the executive and the legislative branches, although judicial rulings are suspected of being based on political considerations rather than on existing law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> However, since May 2014, Thailand has been ruled by a <a href="/wiki/Military_junta" title="Military junta">military junta</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Council_for_Peace_and_Order" title="National Council for Peace and Order">National Council for Peace and Order</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Democracy_Monument_at_night,_BKK.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3828" data-file-width="5743" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Democracy_Monument_at_night%2C_BKK.jpg/220px-Democracy_Monument_at_night%2C_BKK.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Democracy_Monument_at_night%2C_BKK.jpg/330px-Democracy_Monument_at_night%2C_BKK.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Democracy_Monument_at_night%2C_BKK.jpg/440px-Democracy_Monument_at_night%2C_BKK.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Democracy_Monument_at_night,_BKK.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bangkok\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Democracy_Monument,_Bangkok" title="Democracy Monument, Bangkok">Democracy Monument</a>: a representation of the 1932 Constitution sits on top of two golden <a href="/wiki/Phan_(tray)" title="Phan (tray)">offering bowls</a> above a turret.</div></div></div>\n<p>Thailand has had 20 constitutions and charters since 1932, including the latest and current 2017 Constitution. Throughout this time, the form of government has ranged from military dictatorship to electoral democracy, but all governments have acknowledged a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Kings_of_Thailand" title="List of Kings of Thailand">hereditary monarch</a> as the head of state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-multiple_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-multiple-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Thailand has had the 4th most <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d\'&#233;tat">coups</a> in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> "Uniformed or ex-military men have led Thailand for 55 of the 83 years" between 1932 and 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The legislative according to 2007 Constitution was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bicameral" title="Bicameral">bicameral</a> <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Thailand" title="National Assembly of Thailand">National Assembly</a> composed of the <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Thailand" title="Senate of Thailand">Senate</a>, the 150-member <a href="/wiki/Upper_house" title="Upper house">upper house</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/House_of_Representatives_of_Thailand" title="House of Representatives of Thailand">House of Representatives</a>, the 350-member <a href="/wiki/Lower_house" title="Lower house">lower house</a>. Since 2014 coup, it was replaced by a <a href="/wiki/Rubber_stamp_(politics)" title="Rubber stamp (politics)">rubber stamp</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unicameral" title="Unicameral">unicameral</a> <a href="/wiki/National_Legislative_Assembly_of_Thailand_(2014)" title="National Legislative Assembly of Thailand (2014)">National Legislative Assembly</a>.\n</p><p>The current King of Thailand is <a href="/wiki/Vajiralongkorn" title="Vajiralongkorn">Vajiralongkorn</a> (or Rama X) since October 2016. Under the constitution the powers of the king are limited and he is primarily a symbol of the Thai nation. As the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>, he is given some powers and has a role to play in the workings of government. According to the constitution, the king is head of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Thai_Armed_Forces" title="Royal Thai Armed Forces">armed forces</a>. He is required to be Buddhist as well as the defender of all faiths in the country. The king also retained some traditional powers such as the power to appoint his heirs, the power to grant pardons, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Assent" title="Royal Assent">royal assent</a>. The king is aided in his duties by the <a href="/wiki/Privy_Council_of_Thailand" title="Privy Council of Thailand">Privy Council of Thailand</a>.\n</p><p>Since the 2000s, two political parties dominated Thai general elections: one was <a href="/wiki/Pheu_Thai_Party" title="Pheu Thai Party">Pheu Thai Party</a> (which was a successor of <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Power_Party_(Thailand)" title="People\'s Power Party (Thailand)">People\'s Power Party</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thai_Rak_Thai_Party" title="Thai Rak Thai Party">Thai Rak Thai Party</a> respectively) and the other was <a href="/wiki/Democrat_Party_(Thailand)" title="Democrat Party (Thailand)">Democrat Party</a>. The political parties which support <a href="/wiki/Thaksin_Shinawatra" title="Thaksin Shinawatra">Thaksin Shinawatra</a> won the most representatives every general election since 2001. In a controversial move, the pro-army \n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Domestic_human_rights">Domestic human rights</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Thailand" title="Human rights in Thailand">Human rights in Thailand</a> and <a href="/wiki/L%C3%A8se_majest%C3%A9_in_Thailand" title="L&#232;se majest&#233; in Thailand">L&#232;se majest&#233; in Thailand</a></div>\n<p>The 2007 constitution was partially abrogated by the <a href="/wiki/Military_dictatorship" title="Military dictatorship">military dictatorship</a> that came to power in May 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Thailand\'s kings are protected by <i><a href="/wiki/L%C3%A8se-majest%C3%A9" title="L&#232;se-majest&#233;">l&#232;se-majest&#233;</a></i> laws which allows critics to be jailed for three to fifteen years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/2014_Thai_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="2014 Thai coup d\'&#233;tat">2014 Thai coup d\'&#233;tat</a>, Thailand had the highest number of l&#232;se-majest&#233; prisoners in the nation\'s history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-independent_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-independent-47">[47]</a></sup> In 2017, the military court in Thailand sentenced a man to 35 years in prison for violating the country\'s l&#232;se-majest&#233; law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-independent_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-independent-47">[47]</a></sup> Thailand has been rated <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freedom_in_the_World_(report)" title="Freedom in the World (report)">not free</a></i> on the <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a> Index since 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Thai activist and magazine editor <a href="/wiki/Somyot_Prueksakasemsuk" title="Somyot Prueksakasemsuk">Somyot Prueksakasemsuk</a>, who was sentenced to eleven years\' imprisonment for <i>l&#232;se-majest&#233;</i> in 2013,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> is a designated <a href="/wiki/Prisoner_of_conscience" title="Prisoner of conscience">prisoner of conscience</a> by Amnesty International.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Thailand" title="Geography of Thailand">Geography of Thailand</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nan_z_doi_phuka_2006_1003.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="506" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Nan_z_doi_phuka_2006_1003.jpg/220px-Nan_z_doi_phuka_2006_1003.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Nan_z_doi_phuka_2006_1003.jpg/330px-Nan_z_doi_phuka_2006_1003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Nan_z_doi_phuka_2006_1003.jpg/440px-Nan_z_doi_phuka_2006_1003.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nan_z_doi_phuka_2006_1003.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View of the <a href="/wiki/Luang_Prabang_Range" title="Luang Prabang Range">Luang Prabang Range</a>, which straddles the Thai-Lao border, in <a href="/wiki/Nan_Province" title="Nan Province">Nan Province</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Thailand" title="Northern Thailand">Northern Thailand</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Totalling 513,120 square kilometres (198,120&#160;sq&#160;mi),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> Thailand is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area" title="List of countries and dependencies by area">50th-largest country</a> by total area. It is slightly smaller than <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a> and slightly larger than <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>.\n</p><p>Thailand comprises several distinct geographic regions, partly corresponding to the provincial groups. The north of the country is the mountainous area of the <a href="/wiki/Thai_highlands" title="Thai highlands">Thai highlands</a>, with the highest point being <a href="/wiki/Doi_Inthanon" title="Doi Inthanon">Doi Inthanon</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Thanon_Thong_Chai_Range" title="Thanon Thong Chai Range">Thanon Thong Chai Range</a> at 2,565 metres (8,415&#160;ft) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a>. The northeast, <a href="/wiki/Isan" title="Isan">Isan</a>, consists of the <a href="/wiki/Khorat_Plateau" title="Khorat Plateau">Khorat Plateau</a>, bordered to the east by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mekong_River" title="Mekong River">Mekong River</a>.
