The centre of the country is dominated by the predominantly flat <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chao_Phraya" title="Chao Phraya">Chao Phraya</a> river valley, which runs into the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Thailand" title="Gulf of Thailand">Gulf of Thailand</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Thailand_06_-_40_Railay_(158632937).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Thailand_06_-_40_Railay_%28158632937%29.jpg/220px-Thailand_06_-_40_Railay_%28158632937%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Thailand_06_-_40_Railay_%28158632937%29.jpg/330px-Thailand_06_-_40_Railay_%28158632937%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Thailand_06_-_40_Railay_%28158632937%29.jpg/440px-Thailand_06_-_40_Railay_%28158632937%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Thailand_06_-_40_Railay_(158632937).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A typical limestone island in Thailand</div></div></div>\n<p>Southern Thailand consists of the narrow <a href="/wiki/Kra_Isthmus" title="Kra Isthmus">Kra Isthmus</a> that widens into the <a href="/wiki/Malay_Peninsula" title="Malay Peninsula">Malay Peninsula</a>. Politically, there are six geographical regions which differ from the others in population, basic resources, natural features, and level of social and economic development. The diversity of the regions is the most pronounced attribute of Thailand\'s physical setting.\n</p><p>The Chao Phraya and the Mekong River are the indispensable water courses of rural Thailand. Industrial scale production of crops use both rivers and their tributaries. The Gulf of Thailand covers 320,000 square kilometres (124,000&#160;sq&#160;mi) and is fed by the Chao Phraya, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mae_Klong_River" title="Mae Klong River">Mae Klong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bang_Pakong_River" title="Bang Pakong River">Bang Pakong</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tapi_River,_Thailand" title="Tapi River, Thailand">Tapi</a> Rivers. It contributes to the tourism sector owing to its clear shallow waters along the coasts in the southern region and the Kra Isthmus. The eastern shore of the Gulf of Thailand is an industrial centre of Thailand with the kingdom\'s premier deepwater port in <a href="/wiki/Sattahip_District" title="Sattahip District">Sattahip</a> and its busiest commercial port, <a href="/wiki/Laem_Chabang" title="Laem Chabang">Laem Chabang</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Isla_Phi_Phi_Lay,_Tailandia,_2013-08-19,_DD_04.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3252" data-file-width="5144" decoding="async" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Isla_Phi_Phi_Lay%2C_Tailandia%2C_2013-08-19%2C_DD_04.JPG/220px-Isla_Phi_Phi_Lay%2C_Tailandia%2C_2013-08-19%2C_DD_04.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Isla_Phi_Phi_Lay%2C_Tailandia%2C_2013-08-19%2C_DD_04.JPG/330px-Isla_Phi_Phi_Lay%2C_Tailandia%2C_2013-08-19%2C_DD_04.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Isla_Phi_Phi_Lay%2C_Tailandia%2C_2013-08-19%2C_DD_04.JPG/440px-Isla_Phi_Phi_Lay%2C_Tailandia%2C_2013-08-19%2C_DD_04.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Isla_Phi_Phi_Lay,_Tailandia,_2013-08-19,_DD_04.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Phi_Phi_Islands" title="Phi Phi Islands">Phi Phi Islands</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Andaman_Sea" title="Andaman Sea">Andaman Sea</a> is a precious natural resource as it hosts the most popular and luxurious resorts in Asia. <a href="/wiki/Phuket_Province" title="Phuket Province">Phuket</a>, <a href="/wiki/Krabi" title="Krabi">Krabi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ranong" title="Ranong">Ranong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phang_Nga" title="Phang Nga">Phang Nga</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trang_Province" title="Trang Province">Trang</a>, and their islands, all lay along the coasts of the Andaman Sea and, despite the <a href="/wiki/2004_Indian_Ocean_earthquake_and_tsunami" title="2004 Indian Ocean earthquake and tsunami">2004 tsunami</a>, they remain a tourist magnet for visitors from around the world.\n</p><p>Plans have resurfaced for <a href="/wiki/Thai_Canal" title="Thai Canal">a canal</a> which would connect the Andaman Sea to the Gulf of Thailand, analogous to the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Panama_Canal" title="Panama Canal">Panama Canals</a>. The idea has been greeted positively by Thai politicians as it would cut fees charged by the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Singapore" title="Port of Singapore">Ports of Singapore</a>, improve ties with China and India, lower shipping times, and eliminate pirate attacks in the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Malacca" title="Strait of Malacca">Strait of Malacca</a>, and support the Thai government\'s policy of being the logistical hub for Southeast Asia. The canal, it is claimed, would improve economic conditions in the south of Thailand, which relies heavily on tourism income, and it would also change the structure of the Thai economy by making it an Asia logistical hub. The canal would be a major engineering project and has an expected cost of US$20&#8211;30 billion.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Thailand_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1900" data-file-width="1258" decoding="async" height="332" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Thailand_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/220px-Thailand_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Thailand_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/330px-Thailand_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Thailand_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/440px-Thailand_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Thailand_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Thailand map of K&#246;ppen climate classification</div></div></div>\n<p>Thailand\'s climate is influenced by monsoon winds that have a seasonal character (the southwest and northeast monsoon).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tmd_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-tmd-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>2</span></sup> The southwest monsoon, which starts from May until October is characterized by movement of warm, moist air from the Indian Ocean to Thailand, causing abundant rain over most of the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tmd_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-tmd-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>2</span></sup> The northeast monsoon, starting from October until February brings cold and dry air from China over most of Thailand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tmd_51-2"><a href="#cite_note-tmd-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>2</span></sup> In southern Thailand, the northeast monsoon brings mild weather and abundant rainfall on the eastern coast of that region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tmd_51-3"><a href="#cite_note-tmd-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>2</span></sup> Most of Thailand has a "tropical wet and dry or savanna climate" type (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K&#246;ppen climate classification">K&#246;ppen</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Tropical_savanna_climate" title="Tropical savanna climate">Tropical savanna climate</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> The south and the eastern tip of the east have a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_monsoon_climate" title="Tropical monsoon climate">tropical monsoon climate</a>.\n</p><p>Thailand is divided into three seasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tmd_51-4"><a href="#cite_note-tmd-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>2</span></sup> The first is the rainy or southwest monsoon season (mid&#8211;May to mid&#8211;October) which prevails over most of the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tmd_51-5"><a href="#cite_note-tmd-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>2</span></sup> This season is characterized by abundant rain with August and September being the wettest period of the year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tmd_51-6"><a href="#cite_note-tmd-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>2</span></sup> This can occasionally lead to floods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tmd_51-7"><a href="#cite_note-tmd-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>4</span></sup> In addition to rainfall caused by the southwest monsoon, the <a href="/wiki/Intertropical_Convergence_Zone" title="Intertropical Convergence Zone">Intertropical Convergence Zone</a> (ITCZ)  and tropical <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cyclones" title="Cyclones">cyclones</a> also contribute to producing heavy rainfall during the rainy season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tmd_51-8"><a href="#cite_note-tmd-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>2</span></sup> Nonetheless, dry spells commonly occur for 1 to 2 weeks from June to early July.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tmd_51-9"><a href="#cite_note-tmd-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>4</span></sup> This is due to the northward movement of the Intertropical Convergence Zone to southern China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tmd_51-10"><a href="#cite_note-tmd-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>4</span></sup> Winter or the northeast monsoon starts from mid&#8211;October until mid&#8211;February.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tmd_51-11"><a href="#cite_note-tmd-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>2</span></sup> Most of Thailand experiences dry weather during this season with mild temperatures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tmd_51-12"><a href="#cite_note-tmd-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>2</span></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>4</span></sup> The exception is the southern parts of Thailand where it receives abundant rainfall, particularly during October to November.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tmd_51-13"><a href="#cite_note-tmd-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>2</span></sup> Summer or the pre&#8211;monsoon season runs from mid&#8211;February until mid&#8211;May and is characterized by warmer weather.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tmd_51-14"><a href="#cite_note-tmd-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>3</span></sup>\n</p><p>Due to its inland nature and latitude, the north, northeast, central and eastern parts of Thailand experience a long period of warm weather.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tmd_51-15"><a href="#cite_note-tmd-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>3</span></sup> During the hottest time of the year (March to May), temperatures usually reach up to 40&#160;&#176;C (104&#160;&#176;F) or more with the exception of coastal areas where sea breezes moderate afternoon temperatures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tmd_51-16"><a href="#cite_note-tmd-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>3</span></sup> In contrast, outbreaks of cold air from China can bring colder temperatures; in some cases (particularly the north and northeast) close to or below 0&#160;&#176;C (32&#160;&#176;F).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tmd_51-17"><a href="#cite_note-tmd-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>3</span></sup> Southern Thailand is characterized by mild weather year-round with less diurnal and seasonal variations in temperatures due to maritime influences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tmd_51-18"><a href="#cite_note-tmd-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>3</span></sup>\n</p><p>Most of the country receives a mean annual rainfall of 1,200 to 1,600&#160;mm (47 to 63&#160;in).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tmd_51-19"><a href="#cite_note-tmd-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>4</span></sup> However, certain areas on the windward sides of mountains such as Ranong province in the west coast of southern Thailand and eastern parts of Trat Province receive more than 4,500&#160;mm (180&#160;in) of rainfall per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tmd_51-20"><a href="#cite_note-tmd-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>4</span></sup> The driest areas are on the leeward side in the central valleys and northernmost portion of south Thailand where mean annual rainfall is less than 1,200&#160;mm (47&#160;in).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tmd_51-21"><a href="#cite_note-tmd-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>4</span></sup> Most of Thailand (north, northeast, central and east) is characterized by dry weather during the northeast monsoon and abundant rainfall during the southwest monsoon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tmd_51-22"><a href="#cite_note-tmd-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>4</span></sup> In the southern parts of Thailand, abundant rainfall occurs in both the northeast and southwest monsoon seasons with a peak in September for the western coast and a peak in November&#8211;January on the eastern coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tmd_51-23"><a href="#cite_note-tmd-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>4</span></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span></h3>\n<p>Thailand has a mediocre but improving performance in the global <a href="/wiki/Environmental_Performance_Index" title="Environmental Performance Index">Environmental Performance Index</a> (EPI) with an overall ranking of 91 out of 180 countries in 2016. This is also a mediocre rank in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asia_Pacific" title="Asia Pacific">Asia Pacific</a> region specifically, but ahead of countries like Indonesia and China. The EPI was established in 2001 by the <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">World Economic Forum</a> as a global gauge to measure how well individual countries perform in implementing the United Nations\' <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goals" title="Sustainable Development Goals">Sustainable Development Goals</a>. The environmental areas where Thailand performs worst (i.e. highest ranking) are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Air_quality" title="Air quality">air quality</a> (167), environmental effects of the agricultural industry (106) and the <a href="/wiki/Climate_and_energy" title="Climate and energy">climate and energy</a> sector (93), the later mainly because of a high <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CO2_emission" title="CO2 emission">CO2 emission</a> per KWh produced. Thailand performs best (i.e. lowest ranking) in <a href="/wiki/Water_resource_management" title="Water resource management">water resource management</a> (66), with some major improvements expected for the future too, and <a href="/wiki/Sanitation" title="Sanitation">sanitation</a> (68).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_species_native_to_Thailand" title="List of species native to Thailand">List of species native to Thailand</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Khaoyai_06.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2766" data-file-width="4148" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Khaoyai_06.jpg/220px-Khaoyai_06.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Khaoyai_06.jpg/330px-Khaoyai_06.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Khaoyai_06.jpg/440px-Khaoyai_06.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Khaoyai_06.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The population of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_elephants" title="Asian elephants">Asian elephants</a> in Thailand\'s wild has dropped to an estimated 2,000&#8211;3,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TECC_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-TECC-55">[55]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Elephant" title="Elephant">elephant</a> is Thailand\'s <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_animals" title="List of national animals">national symbol</a>. Although there were 100,000 domesticated elephants in Thailand in 1850, the population of elephants has dropped to an estimated 2,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TECC_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-TECC-55">[55]</a></sup> Poachers have long hunted elephants for <a href="/wiki/Ivory" title="Ivory">ivory</a> and hides, and now increasingly for <a href="/wiki/Elephant_meat" title="Elephant meat">meat</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Young elephants are often captured for use in tourist attractions or as work animals, although their use has declined since the government banned <a href="/wiki/Logging" title="Logging">logging</a> in 1989. There are now more elephants in captivity than in the wild, and environmental activists claim that elephants in captivity are often mistreated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Poaching of protected species remains a major problem. Hunters have decimated the populations of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tigers" title="Tigers">tigers</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leopards" title="Leopards">leopards</a>, and other large cats for their valuable pelts. Many animals (including tigers, bears, <a href="/wiki/Crocodile" title="Crocodile">crocodiles</a>, and <a href="/wiki/King_cobra" title="King cobra">king cobras</a>) are farmed or hunted for their meat, which is considered a delicacy, and for their supposed medicinal properties. Although such trade is illegal, the famous Bangkok market <a href="/wiki/Chatuchak_Weekend_Market" title="Chatuchak Weekend Market">Chatuchak</a> is still known for the sale of endangered species.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The practice of keeping wild animals as pets threatens several species. Baby animals are typically captured and sold, which often requires killing the mother. Once in captivity and out of their natural habitat, many pets die or fail to reproduce. Affected populations include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asiatic_black_bear" title="Asiatic black bear">Asiatic black bear</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Malayan_sun_bear" title="Malayan sun bear">Malayan sun bear</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lar_gibbon" title="Lar gibbon">white-handed lar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pileated_gibbon" title="Pileated gibbon">pileated gibbon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Binturong" title="Binturong">binturong</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tscwa_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-tscwa-59">[59]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_the_government_of_Thailand" title="Organization of the government of Thailand">Organization of the government of Thailand</a> and <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Thailand" title="Provinces of Thailand">Provinces of Thailand</a></div>\n<p>Thailand is divided into 76 <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Thailand" title="Provinces of Thailand">provinces</a> (<span lang="th" title="Thai language text">&#3592;&#3633;&#3591;&#3627;&#3623;&#3633;&#3604;</span>, changwat), which are gathered into five groups of provinces by location. There are also two specially-governed districts: the capital <a href="/wiki/Bangkok" title="Bangkok">Bangkok</a> (Krung Thep Maha Nakhon) and <a href="/wiki/Pattaya" title="Pattaya">Pattaya</a>. Bangkok is at provincial level and thus often counted as a province.\n</p><p>Each province is divided into <a href="/wiki/Amphoe" title="Amphoe">districts</a> and the districts are further divided into sub-districts (tambons). As of  2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Thailand&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> there were 878 <a href="/wiki/Amphoe" title="Amphoe">districts (&#3629;&#3635;&#3648;&#3616;&#3629;, amphoe)</a> and the 50 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Districts_of_Bangkok" title="Districts of Bangkok">districts of Bangkok</a> (<span lang="th" title="Thai language text">&#3648;&#3586;&#3605;</span>, khet), which is further divided into 7,255 [[Tambon|subdistricts (<span lang="th" title="Thai language text">&#3605;&#3635;&#3610;&#3621;</span>, tambon)]] in the 76 provinces or <a href="/wiki/Khwaeng" title="Khwaeng">Bangkok\'s subdistricts (&#3649;&#3586;&#3623;&#3591;, khwaeng)</a>. Some parts of the provinces bordering Bangkok are also referred to as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bangkok_Metropolitan_Area" title="Bangkok Metropolitan Area">Greater Bangkok</a> (<span lang="th" title="Thai language text">&#3611;&#3619;&#3636;&#3617;&#3603;&#3601;&#3621;</span>, pari monthon). These provinces include <a href="/wiki/Nonthaburi_Province" title="Nonthaburi Province">Nonthaburi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pathum_Thani_Province" title="Pathum Thani Province">Pathum Thani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samut_Prakan_Province" title="Samut Prakan Province">Samut Prakan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nakhon_Pathom_Province" title="Nakhon Pathom Province">Nakhon Pathom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Samut_Sakhon_Province" title="Samut Sakhon Province">Samut Sakhon</a>. The name of each province\'s capital city (<span lang="th" title="Thai language text">&#3648;&#3617;&#3639;&#3629;&#3591;</span>, mueang) is the same as that of the province. For example, the capital of Chiang Mai Province (<i>Changwat Chiang Mai</i>) is <i>Mueang Chiang Mai</i> or <i>Chiang Mai</i>.\n</p>\n<div class="center"><small>A clickable map of Thailand exhibiting its provinces.</small></div>\n<div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><div class="noresize" style="height: 1231px; width: 700px; "><map name="ImageMap_1_286149278"><area alt="Chiang Rai Province" none;"/></a></div></div></div></div>\n<p><br/>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regions">Regions</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Thailand_four_regions.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1849" data-file-width="1051" decoding="async" height="387" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Thailand_four_regions.svg/220px-Thailand_four_regions.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Thailand_four_regions.svg/330px-Thailand_four_regions.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Thailand_four_regions.svg/440px-Thailand_four_regions.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Thailand_four_regions.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Thailand four-region division</div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Thailand" title="Regions of Thailand">Regions of Thailand</a></div>\n<p>Thai provinces are administrated by regions. The regions that Thailand uses to divide the provinces is the four-region division system. It divides the country into the four regions:\n<a href="/wiki/Northern_Thailand" title="Northern Thailand">Northern Thailand</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northeastern_Thailand" title="Northeastern Thailand">Northeastern Thailand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_Thailand" title="Central Thailand">Central Thailand</a>\nand <a href="/wiki/Southern_Thailand" title="Southern Thailand">Southern Thailand</a>. Each region has its own different historical background, culture, language and people.\n</p><p>In contrast to the <a href="/wiki/Administrative_division" title="Administrative division">administrative divisions</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Thailand" title="Provinces of Thailand">Provinces of Thailand</a>, Thailand is a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">Unitary state</a>, the provincial Governors, district chiefs, and district clerks are appointed by the central government. The regions themselves do not have an administrative character, but are used for <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Thailand" title="Geography of Thailand">geographical</a>, <a href="/wiki/Statistics" title="Statistics">statistical</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geology" title="Geology">geological</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meteorology" title="Meteorology">meteorological</a> or <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">touristic</a> purposes.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Southern_region">Southern region</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/South_Thailand_insurgency" title="South Thailand insurgency">South Thailand insurgency</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Souththailandmap.GIF"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="319" data-file-width="468" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Souththailandmap.GIF/220px-Souththailandmap.GIF" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Souththailandmap.GIF/330px-Souththailandmap.GIF 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Souththailandmap.GIF/440px-Souththailandmap.GIF 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Souththailandmap.GIF" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Southern provinces of Thailand showing the Malay-Muslim majority areas</div></div></div>\n<p>Thailand controlled the <a href="/wiki/Malay_Peninsula" title="Malay Peninsula">Malay Peninsula</a> as far south as Malacca in the 15th century and held much of the peninsula, including Temasek (Singapore), some of the <a href="/wiki/Andaman_Islands" title="Andaman Islands">Andaman Islands</a>, and a colony on <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a>, but eventually contracted when the British used force to guarantee their <a href="/wiki/Suzerainty" title="Suzerainty">suzerainty</a> over the sultanate.\n</p><p>Mostly the northern states of the Malay Sultanate presented annual gifts to the Thai king in the form of a <a href="/wiki/Bunga_mas" title="Bunga mas">golden flower</a>&#8212;a gesture of tribute and an acknowledgement of vassalage. The British intervened in the Malay State and with the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Siamese_Treaty_of_1909" title="Anglo-Siamese Treaty of 1909">Anglo-Siamese Treaty</a> tried to build a railway from the south to Bangkok. Thailand relinquished sovereignty over what are now the northern Malay provinces of <a href="/wiki/Kedah" title="Kedah">Kedah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Perlis" title="Perlis">Perlis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kelantan" title="Kelantan">Kelantan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Terengganu" title="Terengganu">Terengganu</a> to the British. Satun and Pattani Provinces were given to Thailand.\n</p><p>The Malay peninsular provinces were occupied by the Japanese during World War II, and infiltrated by the <a href="/wiki/Malayan_Communist_Party" title="Malayan Communist Party">Malayan Communist Party</a> (CPM) from 1942 to 2008, when they sued for peace with the Malaysian and Thai governments after the CPM lost its support from <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> and China subsequent to the <a href="/wiki/Cultural_Revolution" title="Cultural Revolution">Cultural Revolution</a>. Recent insurgent uprisings may be a continuation of separatist fighting which started after World War II with Sukarno\'s support for the <a href="/wiki/Patani_United_Liberation_Organisation" title="Patani United Liberation Organisation">PULO</a>.  Most victims since the uprisings have been Buddhist and Muslim bystanders.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Thailand" title="Foreign relations of Thailand">Foreign relations of Thailand</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rama_IX_of_Thailand_and_Barack_Obama.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2731" data-file-width="4096" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Rama_IX_of_Thailand_and_Barack_Obama.jpg/220px-Rama_IX_of_Thailand_and_Barack_Obama.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Rama_IX_of_Thailand_and_Barack_Obama.jpg/330px-Rama_IX_of_Thailand_and_Barack_Obama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Rama_IX_of_Thailand_and_Barack_Obama.jpg/440px-Rama_IX_of_Thailand_and_Barack_Obama.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rama_IX_of_Thailand_and_Barack_Obama.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>King <a href="/wiki/Bhumibol_Adulyadej" title="Bhumibol Adulyadej">Bhumibol Adulyadej</a> in a meeting with U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>, 18 November 2012</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Royal_Thai_Embassy_Wellington_New_Zealand_2015.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="931" data-file-width="1613" decoding="async" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Royal_Thai_Embassy_Wellington_New_Zealand_2015.JPG/220px-Royal_Thai_Embassy_Wellington_New_Zealand_2015.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Royal_Thai_Embassy_Wellington_New_Zealand_2015.JPG/330px-Royal_Thai_Embassy_Wellington_New_Zealand_2015.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Royal_Thai_Embassy_Wellington_New_Zealand_2015.JPG/440px-Royal_Thai_Embassy_Wellington_New_Zealand_2015.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Royal_Thai_Embassy_Wellington_New_Zealand_2015.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Royal Thai Embassy in <a href="/wiki/Wellington" title="Wellington">Wellington</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The foreign relations of Thailand are handled by the Minister of Foreign Affairs.\n</p><p>Thailand participates fully in international and regional organisations. It is a <a href="/wiki/Major_non-NATO_ally" title="Major non-NATO ally">major non-NATO ally</a> and Priority Watch List <a href="/wiki/Special_301_Report" title="Special 301 Report">Special 301 Report</a> of the United States. The country remains an active member of ASEAN <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Southeast_Asian_Nations" title="Association of Southeast Asian Nations">Association of Southeast Asian Nations</a>. Thailand has developed increasingly close ties with other ASEAN members: Indonesia, Malaysia, the Philippines, Singapore, Brunei, Laos, Cambodia, Myanmar, and Vietnam, whose foreign and economic ministers hold annual meetings. Regional co-operation is progressing in economic, trade, banking, political, and cultural matters. In 2003, Thailand served as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asia_Pacific_Economic_Cooperation" title="Asia Pacific Economic Cooperation">APEC</a> (Asia Pacific Economic Cooperation) host. Dr. Supachai Panitchpakdi, the former Deputy Prime Minister of Thailand, currently serves as Secretary-General of the United Nations Conference on Trade and Development (UNCTAD). In 2005 Thailand attended the inaugural East Asia Summit.\n</p><p>In recent years, Thailand has taken an increasingly active role on the international stage. When <a href="/wiki/East_Timor" title="East Timor">East Timor</a> gained independence from Indonesia, Thailand, for the first time in its history, contributed troops to the international peacekeeping effort. Its troops remain there today as part of a UN peacekeeping force. As part of its effort to increase international ties, Thailand has reached out to such regional organisations as the Organization of American States (OAS) and the Organisation for Security and Cooperation in Europe (OSCE). Thailand has contributed troops to reconstruction efforts in Afghanistan and Iraq.\n</p><p>Thaksin initiated negotiations for several <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_trade_agreement" title="Free trade agreement">free trade agreements</a> with China, Australia, Bahrain, India, and the US. The latter especially was criticised, with claims that uncompetitive Thai industries could be wiped out.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Thaksin also announced that Thailand would forsake foreign aid, and work with donor countries to assist in the development of neighbours in the Greater Mekong Sub-region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Thaksin sought to position Thailand as a regional leader, initiating various development projects in poorer neighbouring countries like Laos. More controversially, he established close, friendly ties with the Burmese dictatorship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Thailand joined the US-led invasion of Iraq, sending a 423-strong humanitarian contingent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> It withdrew its troops on 10 September 2004. Two Thai soldiers died in Iraq in an insurgent attack.\n</p><p>Abhisit appointed Peoples Alliance for Democracy leader Kasit Piromya as foreign minister. In April 2009, fighting broke out between Thai and Cambodian troops on territory immediately adjacent to the 900-year-old ruins of Cambodia\'s <a href="/wiki/Preah_Vihear_Temple" title="Preah Vihear Temple">Preah Vihear</a> Hindu temple near the border. The Cambodian government claimed its army had killed at least four Thais and captured 10 more, although the Thai government denied that any Thai soldiers were killed or injured. Two Cambodian and three Thai soldiers were killed. Both armies blamed the other for firing first and denied entering the other\'s territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Armed_forces">Armed forces</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Royal_Thai_Armed_Forces" title="Royal Thai Armed Forces">Royal Thai Armed Forces</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DN-SD-03-08801-1-.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="402" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/DN-SD-03-08801-1-.JPG/220px-DN-SD-03-08801-1-.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/DN-SD-03-08801-1-.JPG/330px-DN-SD-03-08801-1-.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/DN-SD-03-08801-1-.JPG/440px-DN-SD-03-08801-1-.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DN-SD-03-08801-1-.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/HTMS_Chakri_Naruebet" title="HTMS Chakri Naruebet">HTMS <i>Chakri Naruebet</i></a>, an <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_carrier" title="Aircraft carrier">aircraft carrier</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Thai_Navy" title="Royal Thai Navy">Royal Thai Navy</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Thai_Armed_Forces" title="Royal Thai Armed Forces">Royal Thai Armed Forces</a> (&#3585;&#3629;&#3591;&#3607;&#3633;&#3614;&#3652;&#3607;&#3618;; <small><a href="/wiki/Royal_Thai_General_System_of_Transcription" title="Royal Thai General System of Transcription">RTGS</a>:&#160;</small><span lang="th-Latn" style="font-style:inherit" title="Thai-language transliteration">Kong Thap Thai</span>) constitute the military of the Kingdom of Thailand. It consists of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Thai_Army" title="Royal Thai Army">Royal Thai Army</a> (&#3585;&#3629;&#3591;&#3607;&#3633;&#3614;&#3610;&#3585;&#3652;&#3607;&#3618;), the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Thai_Navy" title="Royal Thai Navy">Royal Thai Navy</a> (&#3585;&#3629;&#3591;&#3607;&#3633;&#3614;&#3648;&#3619;&#3639;&#3629;&#3652;&#3607;&#3618;), and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Thai_Air_Force" title="Royal Thai Air Force">Royal Thai Air Force</a> (&#3585;&#3629;&#3591;&#3607;&#3633;&#3614;&#3629;&#3634;&#3585;&#3634;&#3624;&#3652;&#3607;&#3618;). It also incorporates various <a href="/wiki/Paramilitary" title="Paramilitary">paramilitary</a> forces.\n</p><p>The Thai Armed Forces have a combined manpower of 306,000 active duty personnel and another 245,000 active reserve personnel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Thailand" title="Monarchy of Thailand">head of the Thai Armed Forces</a> (&#3592;&#3629;&#3617;&#3607;&#3633;&#3614;&#3652;&#3607;&#3618;, <i>Chom Thap Thai</i>) is the king,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> although this position is only nominal. The armed forces are managed by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(Thailand)" title="Ministry of Defence (Thailand)">Ministry of Defence of Thailand</a>, which is headed by the Minister of Defence (a member of the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Thailand" title="Cabinet of Thailand">cabinet of Thailand</a>) and commanded by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Thai_Armed_Forces_Headquarters" title="Royal Thai Armed Forces Headquarters">Royal Thai Armed Forces Headquarters</a>, which in turn is headed by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Commanders_of_the_Royal_Thai_Armed_Forces_Headquarters" title="List of Commanders of the Royal Thai Armed Forces Headquarters">Chief of Defence Forces of Thailand</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> In 2011, Thailand\'s known <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_military_expenditure" title="List of countries by military expenditure">military expenditure</a> totalled approximately US$5.1 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Thailand ranked 16th worldwide in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Military_Strength_Index" title="List of countries by Military Strength Index">Military Strength Index</a> based on the <a href="/wiki/Credit_Suisse" title="Credit Suisse">Credit Suisse</a> report in September 2015.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Royal_Thai_Air_Force_F-16_descends_after_being_refueled_by_a_KC-135.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1320" data-file-width="2630" decoding="async" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Royal_Thai_Air_Force_F-16_descends_after_being_refueled_by_a_KC-135.jpg/220px-Royal_Thai_Air_Force_F-16_descends_after_being_refueled_by_a_KC-135.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Royal_Thai_Air_Force_F-16_descends_after_being_refueled_by_a_KC-135.jpg/330px-Royal_Thai_Air_Force_F-16_descends_after_being_refueled_by_a_KC-135.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Royal_Thai_Air_Force_F-16_descends_after_being_refueled_by_a_KC-135.jpg/440px-Royal_Thai_Air_Force_F-16_descends_after_being_refueled_by_a_KC-135.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Royal_Thai_Air_Force_F-16_descends_after_being_refueled_by_a_KC-135.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Royal Thai Air Force <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/F-16_Fighting_Falcon" title="F-16 Fighting Falcon">F-16 Fighting Falcon</a></div></div></div>\n<p>According to the constitution, serving in the armed forces is a duty of all Thai citizens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> However, only males over the age of 21, who have not gone through reserve training of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Territorial_Defence_Student" title="Territorial Defence Student">Territorial Defence Student</a>, are given the option of volunteering for the armed forces, or participating in the random draft. The candidates are subjected to varying lengths of training, from six months to two years of full-time service, depending on their education, whether they have partially completed the reserve training course, and whether they volunteered prior to the draft date (usually 1 April every year).\n</p><p>Candidates with a recognised bachelor\'s degree serve one year of full-time service if they are conscripted, or six months if they volunteer with the military officer at their district office (&#3626;&#3633;&#3626;&#3604;&#3637;, <i>satsadi</i>). Likewise, the training length is also reduced for those who have partially completed the three-year reserve training course of the Territorial Defence Students (&#3619;.&#3604;., <i>ro do</i>). A person who completed one year out of three will only have to serve full-time for one year. Those who completed two years of reserve training will only have to do six months of full-time training, while those who complete three years or more of reserve training will be exempted entirely.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Thailand" title="Public holidays in Thailand">Royal Thai Armed Forces Day</a> is celebrated on 18 January, commemorating the victory of <a href="/wiki/Naresuan" title="Naresuan">Naresuan</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Ayutthaya_Kingdom" title="Ayutthaya Kingdom">Ayutthaya Kingdom</a> in battle against the <a href="/wiki/Crown_prince" title="Crown prince">crown prince</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Toungoo_dynasty" title="Toungoo dynasty">Toungoo dynasty</a> in 1593.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Thailand" title="Education in Thailand">Education in Thailand</a></div>\n<p>In 2014 the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Literacy_rate" title="Literacy rate">literacy rate</a> was 93.5%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Education is provided by a well-organized school system of kindergartens, primary, lower secondary and upper secondary schools, numerous vocational colleges, and universities. The private sector of education is well developed and significantly contributes to the overall provision of education which the government would not be able to meet with public establishments. Education is compulsory up to and including age 14, with the government providing free education through to age 17.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CUAuditorium.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3636" data-file-width="5454" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/CUAuditorium.jpg/220px-CUAuditorium.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/CUAuditorium.jpg/330px-CUAuditorium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/CUAuditorium.jpg/440px-CUAuditorium.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CUAuditorium.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Chulalongkorn_University" title="Chulalongkorn University">Chulalongkorn University</a>, established in 1917, is the oldest university in Thailand.</div></div></div>\n<p>Teaching relies heavily on <a href="/wiki/Rote_learning" title="Rote learning">rote learning</a> rather than on student-centred methodology. The establishment of reliable and coherent curricula for its primary and secondary schools is subject to such rapid changes that schools and their teachers are not always sure what they are supposed to be teaching, and authors and publishers of textbooks are unable to write and print new editions quickly enough to keep up with the volatility. Issues concerning university entrance has been in constant upheaval for a number of years. Nevertheless, Thai education has seen its greatest progress in the years since 2001. Most of the present generation of students are computer literate. Thailand was ranked 54th out of 56 countries globally for English proficiency, the second-lowest in Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Students in ethnic minority areas score consistently lower in standardised national and international tests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DraperJ2012_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-DraperJ2012-74">[74]</a></sup>\n<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OECDTH2013_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-OECDTH2013-75">[75]</a></sup>\n<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup>\nThis is likely due to unequal allocation of educational resources, weak teacher training, poverty, and low Thai language skill, the language of the tests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DraperJ2012_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-DraperJ2012-74">[74]</a></sup>\n<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup>\n<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%81%E0%B9%80%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%99%E0%B9%82%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%87%E0%B9%80%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%AD%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%A1%E0%B8%8A%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%8D_%E0%B8%A1.%E0%B8%95%E0%B9%89%E0%B8%99.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1440" data-file-width="2560" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%81%E0%B9%80%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%99%E0%B9%82%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%87%E0%B9%80%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%AD%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%A1%E0%B8%8A%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%8D_%E0%B8%A1.%E0%B8%95%E0%B9%89%E0%B8%99.png/220px-%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%81%E0%B9%80%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%99%E0%B9%82%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%87%E0%B9%80%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%AD%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%A1%E0%B8%8A%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%8D_%E0%B8%A1.%E0%B8%95%E0%B9%89%E0%B8%99.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%81%E0%B9%80%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%99%E0%B9%82%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%87%E0%B9%80%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%AD%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%A1%E0%B8%8A%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%8D_%E0%B8%A1.%E0%B8%95%E0%B9%89%E0%B8%99.png/330px-%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%81%E0%B9%80%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%99%E0%B9%82%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%87%E0%B9%80%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%AD%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%A1%E0%B8%8A%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%8D_%E0%B8%A1.%E0%B8%95%E0%B9%89%E0%B8%99.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%81%E0%B9%80%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%99%E0%B9%82%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%87%E0%B9%80%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%AD%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%A1%E0%B8%8A%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%8D_%E0%B8%A1.%E0%B8%95%E0%B9%89%E0%B8%99.png/440px-%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%81%E0%B9%80%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%99%E0%B9%82%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%87%E0%B9%80%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%AD%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%A1%E0%B8%8A%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%8D_%E0%B8%A1.%E0%B8%95%E0%B9%89%E0%B8%99.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%81%E0%B9%80%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%99%E0%B9%82%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%87%E0%B9%80%E0%B8%A3%E0%B8%B5%E0%B8%A2%E0%B8%99%E0%B8%AD%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%AA%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%A1%E0%B8%8A%E0%B8%B1%E0%B8%8D_%E0%B8%A1.%E0%B8%95%E0%B9%89%E0%B8%99.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Thailand is a country where <a href="/wiki/School_uniform" title="School uniform">school uniform</a> is still mandatory.</div></div></div>\n<p>Extensive nationwide <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IQ" title="IQ">IQ</a> tests were administered to 72,780 Thai students from December 2010 to January 2011. The average IQ was found to be 98.59, which is higher than previous studies have found. IQ levels were found to be inconsistent throughout the country, with the lowest average of 88.07 found in the southern region of <a href="/wiki/Narathiwat_Province" title="Narathiwat Province">Narathiwat Province</a> and the highest average of 108.91 reported in <a href="/wiki/Nonthaburi_Province" title="Nonthaburi Province">Nonthaburi Province</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Public_Health_(Thailand)" title="Ministry of Public Health (Thailand)">Ministry of Public Health</a> blames the discrepancies on iodine deficiency and steps are being taken to require that iodine be added to table salt, a practice common in many Western countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2013, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Information_and_Communication_Technology_(Thailand)" title="Ministry of Information and Communication Technology (Thailand)">Ministry of Information and Communication Technology</a> announced that 27,231 schools would receive classroom-level access to <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">high-speed internet</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template"><span style="white-space: nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Link_rot" title="Wikipedia:Link rot"><span title="&#160;Dead link since January 2015">dead link</span></a></i>]</span></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Thai_inventions_and_discoveries" title="List of Thai inventions and discoveries">List of Thai inventions and discoveries</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Thailand_Ministry_of_Information_and_Communication_Technology_2014_Censorship_Image.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1280" decoding="async" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Thailand_Ministry_of_Information_and_Communication_Technology_2014_Censorship_Image.jpg/220px-Thailand_Ministry_of_Information_and_Communication_Technology_2014_Censorship_Image.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Thailand_Ministry_of_Information_and_Communication_Technology_2014_Censorship_Image.jpg/330px-Thailand_Ministry_of_Information_and_Communication_Technology_2014_Censorship_Image.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Thailand_Ministry_of_Information_and_Communication_Technology_2014_Censorship_Image.jpg/440px-Thailand_Ministry_of_Information_and_Communication_Technology_2014_Censorship_Image.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Thailand_Ministry_of_Information_and_Communication_Technology_2014_Censorship_Image.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A screenshot of a censored website displaying words from Thailand\'s Ministry of Information and Communication Technology in 2014</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Science_and_Technology_Development_Agency" title="National Science and Technology Development Agency">National Science and Technology Development Agency</a> is an <a href="/wiki/Government_agency" title="Government agency">agency</a> of the government of Thailand which supports research in science and technology and its application in the <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Thailand" title="Economy of Thailand">Thai economy</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>The Synchrotron Light Research Institute (SLRI) is a Thai <a href="/wiki/Synchrotron_light_source" title="Synchrotron light source">synchrotron light source</a> for physics, chemistry, material science, and life sciences. It is at the <a href="/wiki/Suranaree_University_of_Technology" title="Suranaree University of Technology">Suranaree University of Technology</a> (SUT), in <a href="/wiki/Nakhon_Ratchasima" title="Nakhon Ratchasima">Nakhon Ratchasima</a>, about 300 kilometres (190 miles) northeast of Bangkok. The institute, financed by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Science_and_Technology_(Thailand)" title="Ministry of Science and Technology (Thailand)">Ministry of Science and Technology</a> (MOST), houses the only large scale synchrotron in Southeast Asia. It was originally built as the SORTEC synchrotron in Japan and later moved to Thailand and modified for 1.2 GeV operation. It provides users with regularly scheduled light.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Internet">Internet</span></h3>\n<p>In Bangkok, there are very many free public <a href="/wiki/Wi-Fi" title="Wi-Fi">Wi-Fi</a> Internet hotspots.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Internet_in_Thailand" title="Internet in Thailand">Internet in Thailand</a> includes 10<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gbit" title="Gbit">Gbit</a>/s high speed fibre-optic lines that can be leased and ISPs such as KIRZ that provide residential Internet services.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>The Internet is <a href="/wiki/Internet_censorship_in_Thailand" title="Internet censorship in Thailand">censored</a> by the Thai government, making some sites unreachable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-asiancorrespondent.com_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-asiancorrespondent.com-82">[82]</a></sup> The organisations responsible are the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Thai_Police" title="Royal Thai Police">Royal Thai Police</a>, the <a href="/wiki/CAT_Telecom" title="CAT Telecom">Communications Authority of Thailand</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Information_and_Communication_Technology_(Thailand)" title="Ministry of Information and Communication Technology (Thailand)">Ministry of Information and Communication Technology</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Information_and_Communication_Technology_(Thailand)" title="Ministry of Information and Communication Technology (Thailand)">MICT</a>).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>\n<table class="box-Very_long plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style ambox-very_long" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="" data-file-height="48" data-file-width="48" decoding="async" height="40" 2018</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Thailand" title="Economy of Thailand">Economy of Thailand</a></div>\n<table class="infobox" style="font-size: 90%; border: 1px solid #999; float: right; margin-left: 1em; width:300px">\n<tbody><tr href="#cite_note-nesdb17-84">[84]</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Inflation" title="Inflation">Inflation</a><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">&#8226; Headline</span><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">&#8226; Core</span></td>\n<td><br/>0.7% <span style="font-size:85%;"> (2017)</span><br/>0.6% <span style="font-size:85%;"> (2017)</span></td>\n<td style="text-align:
