class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Thailand" title="Health in Thailand">Health in Thailand</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SIRIRAJ_HOSPITAL_-_panoramio.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/SIRIRAJ_HOSPITAL_-_panoramio.jpg/200px-SIRIRAJ_HOSPITAL_-_panoramio.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/SIRIRAJ_HOSPITAL_-_panoramio.jpg/300px-SIRIRAJ_HOSPITAL_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/SIRIRAJ_HOSPITAL_-_panoramio.jpg/400px-SIRIRAJ_HOSPITAL_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SIRIRAJ_HOSPITAL_-_panoramio.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Siriraj_Hospital" title="Siriraj Hospital">Siriraj Hospital</a> in Bangkok, the oldest and largest hospital in Thailand.</div></div></div>\n<p>Health and medical care is overseen by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Public_Health_(Thailand)" title="Ministry of Public Health (Thailand)">Ministry of Public Health</a> (MOPH), along with several other non-ministerial government agencies, with total national expenditures on health amounting to 4.3 percent of GDP in 2009. <a href="/wiki/Non-communicable_disease" title="Non-communicable disease">Non-communicable diseases</a> form the major burden of morbidity and mortality, while infectious diseases including malaria and tuberculosis, as well as traffic accidents, are also important public health issues.\n</p><p>The current Minister for Public Health is Prof. Emeritus Piyasakol Sakolsatayadorn, M.D. and the Permanent Secretary of Ministry of Public Health is Jedsada Chokdamrongsuk, M.D. <a href="/wiki/Somsak_Chunharas" title="Somsak Chunharas">Somsak Chunharas</a>, MD, MPH, was once Deputy Minister for Public Health and is currently a Senior Leadership Fellow at the <a href="/wiki/Harvard_T.H._Chan_School_of_Public_Health" title="Harvard T.H. Chan School of Public Health">Harvard T.H. Chan School of Public Health</a> in Boston.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In December 2018 the interim parliament voted to legalize the use of cannabis for medical reasons. Recreational use remained unlawful. The National Legislative Assembly had 166 votes in favor of the amendment to the Narcotics Bill, while there were no nay votes and 13 abstentions. The vote makes Thailand the first Southeast Asian country to allow the use of medical marijuana.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Thailand" title="Culture of Thailand">Culture of Thailand</a></div><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Thailand" title="Music of Thailand">Music of Thailand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Isan" title="Isan">Isan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Thailand" title="Cinema of Thailand">Cinema of Thailand</a></div>\n<p>Thai culture has been shaped by many influences, including Indian, Lao, Burmese, Cambodian, and Chinese.\n</p><p>Its traditions incorporate a great deal of influence from India, China, Cambodia, and the rest of Southeast Asia. Thailand\'s national religion, Theravada Buddhism, is central to modern Thai identity. <a href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_Thailand" title="Buddhism in Thailand">Thai Buddhism</a> has evolved over time to include many regional beliefs originating from <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Animism" title="Animism">animism</a>, as well as ancestor worship. The <a href="/wiki/Thai_solar_calendar" title="Thai solar calendar">official calendar</a> in Thailand is based on the Eastern version of the <a href="/wiki/Buddhist_calendar" title="Buddhist calendar">Buddhist Era</a> (BE), which is 543 years ahead of the <a href="/wiki/Gregorian_calendar" title="Gregorian calendar">Gregorian (Western) calendar</a>. Thus the year 2015 is 2558 BE in Thailand.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Silk_Loom_Jim_Thompson_House_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4800" data-file-width="3200" decoding="async" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Silk_Loom_Jim_Thompson_House_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg/140px-Silk_Loom_Jim_Thompson_House_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Silk_Loom_Jim_Thompson_House_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg/210px-Silk_Loom_Jim_Thompson_House_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Silk_Loom_Jim_Thompson_House_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg/280px-Silk_Loom_Jim_Thompson_House_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg 2x" width="140"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Silk_Loom_Jim_Thompson_House_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Thai women wearing <a href="/wiki/Sabai" title="Sabai">sabai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Thompson_House" title="Jim Thompson House">Jim Thompson House</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Several different ethnic groups, many of which are marginalised, populate Thailand. Some of these groups spill over into Myanmar, Laos, Cambodia and Malaysia and have mediated change between their traditional local culture, national Thai, and global cultural influences. <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">Overseas Chinese</a> also form a significant part of Thai society, particularly in and around Bangkok. Their successful integration into Thai society has allowed for this group to hold positions of economic and political power. Thai Chinese businesses prosper as part of the larger <a href="/wiki/Bamboo_network" title="Bamboo network">bamboo network</a>, a network of <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">overseas Chinese</a> businesses operating in the markets of Southeast Asia that share common family and cultural ties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weidenbaum_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-Weidenbaum-139">[139]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Khon_Thammasat_20090306_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1797" data-file-width="2696" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Khon_Thammasat_20090306_01.jpg/220px-Khon_Thammasat_20090306_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Khon_Thammasat_20090306_01.jpg/330px-Khon_Thammasat_20090306_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Khon_Thammasat_20090306_01.jpg/440px-Khon_Thammasat_20090306_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Khon_Thammasat_20090306_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Khon" title="Khon">Khon</a> show is the most stylised form of Thai performance.</div></div></div>\n<p>The traditional Thai greeting, the <i><a href="/wiki/Thai_greeting" title="Thai greeting">wai</a></i>, is generally offered first by the younger of the two people meeting, with their hands pressed together, fingertips pointing upwards as the head is bowed to touch face to fingertips, usually coinciding with the spoken words "sawatdi khrap" for male speakers, and "sawatdi kha" for females. The elder may then respond in the same way. Social status and position, such as in government, will also have an influence on who performs the <i>wai</i> first. For example, although one may be considerably older than a provincial governor, when meeting it is usually the visitor who pays respect first. When children leave to go to school, they are taught to <i>wai</i> their parents to indicate their respect. The wai is a sign of respect and reverence for another, similar to the <a href="/wiki/Namaste" title="Namaste">namaste</a> greeting of India and Nepal.\n</p><p>As with other Asian cultures, respect towards ancestors is an essential part of Thai spiritual practice. Thais have a strong sense of hospitality and generosity, but also a strong sense of social hierarchy. Seniority is paramount in Thai culture. Elders have by tradition ruled in family decisions or ceremonies. Older siblings have duties to younger ones.\n</p><p>Taboos in Thailand include touching someone\'s head or pointing with the feet, as the head is considered the most sacred and the foot the lowest part of the body.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Thailand" title="Cuisine of Thailand">Cuisine of Thailand</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Thai_vegetable_carving.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2500" data-file-width="2500" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Thai_vegetable_carving.jpg/220px-Thai_vegetable_carving.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Thai_vegetable_carving.jpg/330px-Thai_vegetable_carving.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Thai_vegetable_carving.jpg/440px-Thai_vegetable_carving.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Thai_vegetable_carving.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The art of <a href="/wiki/Vegetable_carving" title="Vegetable carving">vegetable carving</a> is thought to have originated in the <a href="/wiki/Sukhothai_Kingdom" title="Sukhothai Kingdom">Sukhothai Kingdom</a> nearly 700 years ago<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Thailand" title="Cuisine of Thailand">Thai cuisine</a> blends five fundamental tastes: sweet, spicy, sour, bitter, and salty. Common ingredients used in Thai cuisine include garlic, chillies, lime juice, lemon grass, <a href="/wiki/Coriander" title="Coriander">coriander</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galangal" title="Galangal">galangal</a>, palm sugar, and <a href="/wiki/Fish_sauce" title="Fish sauce">fish sauce</a> (<i>nam pla</i>). The staple food in Thailand is rice, particularly <a href="/wiki/Jasmine_rice" title="Jasmine rice">jasmine variety rice</a> (also known as "hom Mali" rice) which forms a part of almost every meal. Thailand was long<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (May 2016)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> the world\'s largest exporter of rice, and Thais domestically consume over 100&#160;kg of milled rice per person per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRRI_Thailand_123-1"><a href="#cite_note-IRRI_Thailand-123">[123]</a></sup> Over 5,000 varieties of rice from Thailand are preserved in the rice gene bank of the <a href="/wiki/International_Rice_Research_Institute" title="International Rice Research Institute">International Rice Research Institute</a> (IRRI), based in the Philippines. The king of Thailand is the official patron of IRRI.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Thailand" title="Media of Thailand">Media of Thailand</a></div>\n<p>Thai society has been influenced in recent years by its widely available multi-language press and media. There are some English and numerous Thai and Chinese newspapers in circulation. Most Thai popular magazines use English headlines as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chic_(style)" title="Chic (style)">chic</a> glamour factor. Many large businesses in Bangkok operate in English as well as other languages.\n</p><p>Thailand is the largest newspaper market in Southeast Asia with an estimated circulation of over 13 million copies daily in 2003. Even upcountry, out of Bangkok, the media flourish. For example, according to Thailand\'s Public Relations Department Media Directory 2003&#8211;2004, the nineteen provinces of <a href="/wiki/Isan" title="Isan">Isan</a>, Thailand\'s northeastern region, hosted 116 newspapers along with radio, TV, and cable. Since then, another province, Bueng Kan, was incorporated, totalling twenty provinces. In addition, a military coup on 22 May 2014 led to severe state restrictions on all media and forms of expression.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Units_of_measurement">Units of measurement</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Thai_units_of_measurement" title="Thai units of measurement">Thai units of measurement</a></div>\n<p>Thailand generally uses the <a href="/wiki/Metric_system" title="Metric system">metric system</a>, but <a href="/wiki/Thai_units_of_measurement" title="Thai units of measurement">traditional units of measurement</a> for land area are used, and <a href="/wiki/Imperial_units" title="Imperial units">imperial units</a> of measurement are occasionally used for building materials, such as wood and plumbing fixtures. Years are numbered as B.E. (<a href="/wiki/Thai_solar_calendar" title="Thai solar calendar">Buddhist Era</a>) in educational settings, civil service, government, contracts, and newspaper datelines. However, in banking, and increasingly in industry and commerce, standard Western year (Christian or Common Era) counting is the standard practice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Thailand_at_the_Olympics" title="Thailand at the Olympics">Thailand at the Olympics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union_in_Thailand" title="Rugby union in Thailand">Rugby union in Thailand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golf_in_Thailand" title="Golf in Thailand">Golf in Thailand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Football_in_Thailand" title="Football in Thailand">Football in Thailand</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_sporting_events_held_in_Thailand" title="List of sporting events held in Thailand">List of sporting events held in Thailand</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Thaiknee.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="560" data-file-width="400" decoding="async" height="308" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Thaiknee.jpg/220px-Thaiknee.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Thaiknee.jpg/330px-Thaiknee.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d6/Thaiknee.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Thaiknee.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Muay_Thai" title="Muay Thai">Muay Thai</a>, Thailand\'s signature sport</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Muay_Thai" title="Muay Thai">Muay Thai</a> (<a href="/wiki/Thai_language" title="Thai language">Thai</a>: <span lang="th">&#3617;&#3623;&#3618;&#3652;&#3607;&#3618;</span>, RTGS: Muai Thai, <small></small>&#160;<span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Thai_and_Lao" title="Help:IPA/Thai and Lao">[muaj t&#688;aj]</a></span>, lit. "Thai boxing") is a native form of kickboxing and Thailand\'s signature sport. It incorporates kicks, punches, knees and elbow strikes in a ring with gloves similar to those used in Western boxing and this has led to Thailand gaining medals at the Olympic Games in <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Association football</a> has overtaken muay Thai as the most widely followed sport in contemporary Thai society. <a href="/wiki/Thailand_national_football_team" title="Thailand national football team">Thailand national football team</a> has played the <a href="/wiki/AFC_Asian_Cup" title="AFC Asian Cup">AFC Asian Cup</a> six times and reached the semifinals in <a href="/wiki/1972_AFC_Asian_Cup" title="1972 AFC Asian Cup">1972</a>. The country has hosted the Asian Cup twice, in 1972 and in <a href="/wiki/2007_AFC_Asian_Cup" title="2007 AFC Asian Cup">2007</a>. The 2007 edition was co-hosted together with <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>. It is not uncommon to see Thais cheering their favourite English Premier League teams on television and walking around in replica kit. Another widely enjoyed pastime, and once a competitive sport, is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kite_flying" title="Kite flying">kite flying</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RajamangalaStadium.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/RajamangalaStadium.jpg/220px-RajamangalaStadium.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/RajamangalaStadium.jpg/330px-RajamangalaStadium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/RajamangalaStadium.jpg/440px-RajamangalaStadium.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RajamangalaStadium.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rajamangala_National_Stadium" title="Rajamangala National Stadium">Rajamangala National Stadium</a></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">Volleyball</a> is rapidly growing as one of the most popular sports. The <a href="/wiki/Thailand_women%27s_national_volleyball_team" title="Thailand women\'s national volleyball team">women\'s team</a> has often participated in the <a href="/wiki/FIVB_Volleyball_Women%27s_World_Championship" title="FIVB Volleyball Women\'s World Championship">World Championship</a>, <a href="/wiki/FIVB_Volleyball_Women%27s_World_Cup" title="FIVB Volleyball Women\'s World Cup">World Cup</a>, and <a href="/wiki/FIVB_Volleyball_World_Grand_Prix" title="FIVB Volleyball World Grand Prix">World Grand Prix</a> <a href="/wiki/Asian_Championship" title="Asian Championship">Asian Championship</a>. They have won the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Women%27s_Volleyball_Championship" title="Asian Women\'s Volleyball Championship">Asian Championship</a> twice and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AVC_Cup_for_Women" title="AVC Cup for Women">Asian Cup</a> once. By the success of the women\'s team, the <a href="/wiki/Thailand_men%27s_national_volleyball_team" title="Thailand men\'s national volleyball team">men team</a> has been growing as well.\n</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Takraw" title="Takraw">Takraw</a> (Thai: &#3605;&#3632;&#3585;&#3619;&#3657;&#3629;) is a sport native to Thailand, in which the players hit a rattan ball and are only allowed to use their feet, knees, chest, and head to touch the ball. <a href="/wiki/Sepak_takraw" title="Sepak takraw">Sepak takraw</a> is a form of this sport which is similar to volleyball. The players must volley a ball over a net and force it to hit the ground on the opponent\'s side. It is also a popular sport in other countries in Southeast Asia. A rather similar game but played only with the feet is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buka_ball" title="Buka ball">buka ball</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Snooker" title="Snooker">Snooker</a> has enjoyed increasing popularity in Thailand in recent years, with interest in the game being stimulated by the success of Thai snooker player <a href="/wiki/James_Wattana" title="James Wattana">James Wattana</a> in the 1990s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> Other notable players produced by the country include <a href="/wiki/Ratchayothin_Yotharuck" title="Ratchayothin Yotharuck">Ratchayothin Yotharuck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Noppon_Saengkham" title="Noppon Saengkham">Noppon Saengkham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dechawat_Poomjaeng" title="Dechawat Poomjaeng">Dechawat Poomjaeng</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rugby is also a growing sport in Thailand with the <a href="/wiki/Thailand_national_rugby_union_team" title="Thailand national rugby union team">Thailand national rugby union team</a> rising to be ranked 61st in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> Thailand became the first country in the world to host an international 80 welterweight rugby tournament in 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> The national domestic Thailand Rugby Union (TRU) competition includes several universities and services teams such as <a href="/wiki/Chulalongkorn_University" title="Chulalongkorn University">Chulalongkorn University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mahasarakham_University" title="Mahasarakham University">Mahasarakham University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kasetsart_University" title="Kasetsart University">Kasetsart University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Songkla_University" title="Prince of Songkla University">Prince of Songkla University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thammasat_University" title="Thammasat University">Thammasat University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rangsit_University" title="Rangsit University">Rangsit University</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thai_Police" title="Thai Police">Thai Police</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thai_Army" title="Thai Army">Thai Army</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thai_Navy" title="Thai Navy">Thai Navy</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Thai_Air_Force" title="Royal Thai Air Force">Royal Thai Air Force</a>. Local sports clubs which also compete in the TRU include the British Club of Bangkok, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southerners_Sports_Club_(Bangkok)" title="Southerners Sports Club (Bangkok)">Southerners Sports Club (Bangkok)</a> and the Royal Bangkok Sports Club.\n</p><p>Thailand has been called the golf capital of Asia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> as it is a popular destination for golf.  The country attracts a large number of golfers from Japan, Korea, Singapore, South Africa, and Western countries who come to play golf in Thailand every year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup>  The growing popularity of golf, especially among the middle classes and immigrants, is evident as there are more than 200 world-class golf courses nationwide,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> and some of them are chosen to host PGA and LPGA tournaments, such as <a href="/wiki/Amata_Spring_Country_Club" title="Amata Spring Country Club">Amata Spring Country Club</a>, Alpine Golf and Sports Club, Thai Country Club, and Black Mountain Golf Club.\n</p><p>Basketball is a growing sport in Thailand, especially on the professional sports club level. The Chang Thailand Slammers won the 2011 <a href="/wiki/ASEAN_Basketball_League" title="ASEAN Basketball League">ASEAN Basketball League</a> Championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Thailand_national_basketball_team" title="Thailand national basketball team">Thailand national basketball team</a> had its most successful year at the <a href="/wiki/Basketball_at_the_1966_Asian_Games" title="Basketball at the 1966 Asian Games">1966 Asian Games</a> where it won the silver medal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Other sports in Thailand are slowly growing as the country develops its sporting infrastructure. The success in sports like <a href="/wiki/Powerlifting" title="Powerlifting">weightlifting</a> and <a href="/wiki/Taekwondo" title="Taekwondo">taekwondo</a> at the last two summer Olympic Games has demonstrated that boxing is no longer the only medal option for Thailand.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sporting_venues">Sporting venues</span></h3>\n<p>Thammasat Stadium is a multi-purpose stadium in Bangkok. It is currently used mostly for football matches. The stadium holds 25,000. It is on Thammasat University\'s Rangsit campus. It was built for the <a href="/wiki/1998_Asian_Games" title="1998 Asian Games">1998 Asian Games</a> by construction firm Christiani and Nielsen, the same company that constructed the Democracy Monument in Bangkok.\n</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rajamangala_National_Stadium" title="Rajamangala National Stadium">Rajamangala National Stadium</a> is the biggest sporting arena in Thailand. It currently has a capacity of 65,000. It is in Bang Kapi, Bangkok. The stadium was built in 1998 for the 1998 Asian Games and is the home stadium of the <a href="/wiki/Thailand_national_football_team" title="Thailand national football team">Thailand national football team</a>.\n</p><p>The well-known Lumpini Boxing Stadium will host its final Muay Thai boxing matches on 7 February 2014 after the venue first opened in December 1956. Managed by the Royal Thai Army, the stadium was officially selected for the purpose of muay Thai bouts following a competition that was staged on 15 March 1956. From 11 February 2014, the stadium will relocate to Ram Intra Road, due to the new venue\'s capacity to accommodate audiences of up to 3,500. Foreigners typically pay between 1,000&#8211;2,000 baht to view a match, with prices depending on the location of the seating.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_rankings">International rankings</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/International_rankings_of_Thailand" title="International rankings of Thailand">International rankings of Thailand</a></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="National_identity">National identity</span></h2>\n<p>The Fisheries Department is promoting <i>pla gud</i>, or Siamese fighting fish, as the national fish. Department chief Adisorn Promthep said that the proposal will be submitted to the National Identity Office under the Prime Minister\'s Office for approval. He said that once the status is recognised, fighting fish farming would be promoted which would generate money and create jobs. He added that credible records show that <i>pla gud</i> of the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Betta_splendens" title="Betta splendens">Betta splendens</a></i> species are native to Thailand and were first collected for fighting during the reign of King <a href="/wiki/Rama_III" title="Rama III">Rama III</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>\n<div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" Thailand">Outline of Thailand</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n<div
